The Panchen Lama Initiated the Bodhi Society and Convened the First Preparatory Meeting Yesterday 134

Pass the charter to promote Buddhism as the purpose.

The Bodhi Society, initiated by the Panchen Lama together with prominent figures in this city, held its first preparatory meeting at Yunnan Road at 4 pm yesterday. The details are as follows:

Attendees 135

Huang Hanzhi, Qu Wenliu, Wang Xiaolai, Wen Lanting, Yang Hu (represented by Hou Dachun), Luo Sang Jianzan, Li Dachao, Liu Zhiqi, Chen Yuanbai, Zhao Yiwu, Huang Bodu, Li Jingyu, Du Shaopeng, Yang Zigong, Gao Pengjiu, Guan Jiongzhi, Dabeiyuanmo (represented by Gao Duru), Gao Duru, Sun Yaoshen, Feng Yangshan, Qian Jingping, Mao Yun, and others, more than 30 people in total.

Meeting situation 136

The meeting began with a report by Chairman Qu Wenliu, which roughly stated that the Bodhi Society had been initiated in the north several times but had not been established. This time, the Panchen Lama specially entrusted this matter during the banquet for guests at the Diplomatic Building, hoping that people in Shanghai would work hard to complete it. The purpose of this society is to communicate between the two schools of Esoteric and Exoteric Buddhism, so it promotes Buddhism and benefits all beings, and serves as the foundation for saving the country and the world, etc. Next, Luo Sang Jianzan, the representative sent by the Panchen Lama, reported on the Panchen Lama's intentions: (1) To bring a copy of the Kalachakra Tantra first, and then gradually bring the Tibetan scriptures in the future; (2) To send Yongzheng Buddha to lecture on the scriptures; (3) To subsidize the funds, first raise 2,000 yuan, and then determine according to the situation. Finally, the charter of the society was discussed and passed. Due to lack of time, the election of standing personnel was changed to be decided by the chairman.

The Society's Charter 137

Charter of the Preparatory Committee of the Bodhi Society (Article 1) The name of this association is the Preparatory Committee of the Bodhi Society. (Article 2) The purpose of this association is to promote Buddhism, benefit all beings, and prepare for the Bodhi Society. (Article 3) This association plans the following undertakings in accordance with its purpose: Translation: Translate Sanskrit and Tibetan classics, giving priority to those in urgent need. Transmission: Invite great virtues to preside over the transmission of exoteric and esoteric Buddhist teachings. Learning: Recruit those with great aspirations to receive instruction and learn. Debate: Follow the rules of large monasteries in Tibet, research and discuss to clarify the supreme teachings. Practice: Enable those who have made a vow to practice according to the law in order to attain present realization. Compilation: Compile popular teachings in order to popularize them. Circulation: Engrave and print scriptures and widely distribute them. Benefiting the world: Undertake charitable activities and benefit the world as needed. (Article 4) The preparatory period of this association is temporarily set at three months. (Article 5) This association seeks those who share the same aspirations to take on the initiation, and will widely solicit members after the establishment of the Bodhi Society. (Article 6) The funds of this association will be raised separately by the initiators. (Article 7) The Preparatory Committee of this association shall elect 15 to 25 standing committee members to form a Standing Committee to handle the affairs of this association, and the standing committee members shall mutually elect one chairman and two vice-chairmen to preside over daily affairs. (Article 8) This association shall set up a General Affairs Group, a Fundraising Group, a Solicitation Group, and an Accounting Group, each with one director, two deputy directors, and several staff members. (Article 9) This association shall hold a meeting once a month, the Standing Committee shall hold a meeting once every ten days, and temporary meetings shall be convened by the chairman. (Article 10) The detailed rules of this association shall be formulated separately. (Article 11) This charter shall be implemented upon approval by the Preparatory Committee.

Zhang Ayou, a native of Yuyao, lives in Tangjiawan, Nanshi, working as a laborer. Zhang was unable to sleep in his house due to the hot weather. The night before last, he was resting in the shade in the Tangjiawan small vegetable market. He lay on the ground until about 2 am when suddenly several people violently arrived, holding a sharp ax, to the vegetable market and chopped Zhang Ayou hard on the forehead while he was sound asleep. He bled profusely instantly and was unable to speak. Seeing that the purpose had been achieved, the murderers dispersed and fled. Wang Changrong, the police officer of the 17th Squad of the 2nd District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, arrived after learning about it, but the rioters had disappeared without a trace. Only the wounded man was seen covered in blood, on the verge of death. So he sent him to the Shanghai Hospital in Nanshi for treatment by car. According to the doctor's diagnosis, the injuries were very serious, with excessive blood loss, and his life was in danger. It is said that the injured Zhang Ayou secretly reported to the detectives the arrest of Xiao Heshang, Xiao Suzhou, Cai Gui, and others for theft on June 13 of this year, which caused hatred. A Rickshaw Puller in Gaoqiao Prevented a Public Bus From Driving. The Rickshaw Puller Obstructed the Public Bus From Driving and Was Detained. The Vehicle Traffic Was Temporarily Interrupted Until After 6 PM When it Was Restored. 141

The rickshaw pullers in the Gaoqiao area of ​​Pudong clashed with the police officers of the Public Security Bureau yesterday morning over the competition for business with the local public buses, causing the public buses to fail to run and interrupting traffic for several hours. Traffic was not restored until 6:30 pm. The details are listed below:

Cause of the accident 142

After the opening of the seaside bathing beach in Gaoqiao, the rickshaw business was quite good. Soon, the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities set up a public bus in the area. Because the price was low, fast and stable, the rickshaw industry was considerably affected. The rickshaw pullers were quite dissatisfied with this. Yesterday was Sunday, and the Shanghai Qunyi Gongji Science Society was also testing the water safety belt for the first time in the area, so there were more tourists than in the past. At 11 am yesterday, the city ferry that departed from the Bund Bronze Man Pier in Shanghai reached Gaoqiao. At that time, the rickshaw pullers and the public buses of the Bureau of Public Utilities in Gaoqiao Wharf competed for business, did not obey the order, and went forward to solicit business from the passengers, making it impossible for the public buses in the area to drive. The police officers stepped forward to stop them, but the rickshaw pullers did not comply. The police officers then detained two rickshaw pullers from the Yuelai Rickshaw Company and detained them in the Fourth Branch of the Third District of the Public Security Bureau.

Conflict Situation 143

After this incident, the rickshaw pullers all felt a sense of unity, and were quite angry. So they gathered dozens of companions and went to the front of the public bus station in Gaoqiao, pushing the rickshaws and wheelbarrows they used in front of the bus station to prevent the bus from running. The rickshaw pullers have always hated the bus for hindering their business, so they took this opportunity to make both sides unable to receive tourists. At that time, there were about 50 or 60 vehicles obstructing the road. The time was at 11:45 am, and vehicle traffic was completely interrupted. The tourists were quite tired from traveling back and forth under the scorching sun because the Gaoqiao pier was quite far from the seaside bathing beach, and they all complained.

Each suffered minor injuries 144

However, in order to maintain traffic, the public bus contacted the Fourth Branch of the Third District, and the higher authorities dispatched a squad of police officers from the Water Public Security Bureau, who arrived at the station. At this time, the rickshaw pullers even carried several huge square bricks and placed them in the road to block the bus. The police officers dispersed them, but they did not leave. They pulled out their police batons and carried out the expulsion. The rickshaw pullers rushed forward and punched them with their bare hands. Seeing that the number of police officers was too small, they urgently took out their guns and fired warning shots into the sky. As a result, several people on both sides were injured. At 12:15 pm, the rickshaw pullers retreated, and the disturbance temporarily subsided. However, the rickshaw pullers still stacked their vehicles in the road, and the public buses temporarily stopped traffic to avoid disputes. However, at that time, six or seven rickshaw pullers were arrested and taken to the police station.

Temporary Solution 145

At the same time, the bus company sent representatives to negotiate with the rickshaw pullers' association. Then, local people came forward to mediate. As a result, the rickshaw pullers automatically cancelled the obstruction to traffic at 6 pm, and the public buses resumed traffic at 6:30 pm. The arrested rickshaw pullers can be expected to be released. Therefore, the tourists who went to Gaoqiao yesterday almost could not return to Shanghai, and they did not arrive at this city until after 8 pm.

The Grand Production of the Bank of China Research Office, the Banking Yearbook, is Published. The Book Contains 2.5 Million Words and is Divided into 15 Chapters. It is Extremely Detailed on Bank Surveys, Regulations, and Statistics. 146

The Economic Research Office of the General Management Office of the Bank of China has always spared no effort in economic surveys. The various statistics and books compiled have made many contributions to financial and economic issues. Recently, Dr. Zhang Xiaomei, the director of the office, and his colleagues, in view of the fact that the banking industry in our country has always lacked complete and systematic records and statistics, took one year to compile a 1934 National Banking Yearbook for research, which was published on the first of this month. The book contains 2.5 million words, divided into two parts, with a total of 15 chapters and 1,800 pages. It is extremely detailed on the major events of the bank in the past three years, a brief description of the national bank, an overview of the banks in various places, a survey of banking associations, banking regulations, banking statistics, a directory of bank personnel, a bank log, foreign banks, money shops and silver houses, trust companies, silver companies, savings associations, insurance companies, and pawnshops. It can be said to be an unprecedented masterpiece in the banking industry. In order to understand the actual situation of this work, the reporter has extracted the origin and process of the compilation of the Banking Yearbook by the office as follows:

The banking industry in our country has only been developing for 40 years from its germination to the present. Although its achievements cannot be compared with the European and American banking industries with hundreds of years of history, it is still one of the large and new types of enterprises in our country and has attracted the attention of people all over the country. Especially in recent years, the relationship between the bankruptcy of the rural economy and the banking industry has been the focus of researchers. However, due to the complexity of the relationship, the vast scope, and the lack of statistical figures, researchers have no way to start. They have no choice but to use the fragmented information in general newspapers as the basis for their arguments, which often fails to grasp the whole picture. This is what bank scholars deeply feel painful about, and this office has also long been aware of this. However, because this matter is of great importance, it is by no means possible to accomplish it with a small number of human and financial resources, and it cannot be done without a long period of preparation and research. Therefore, starting from 1931, we tried to compile a recent 10-year business overview of national banks, making a systematic analysis and compilation of facts, and publishing it in the Bank of China Monthly, which is published by this office on a regular basis. It was deeply appreciated by people from all walks of life. This office is still not satisfied, so at the beginning of 1932, it selected 26 Shanghai Banking Association member banks with a longer history from the more than 30 banks that had been published, as well as the Central Bank and the Four Bank Savings Association, etc., and reorganized them, adding a brief history, annual, category, notes, index, and charts of each bank, etc., totaling more than 360 pages, which were published at one time, entitled (Research on the Recent 10-Year Business Overview of Important Banks in China), which was published in May 1933. People in the country believed that it was the only reliable data and statistics for studying the banking industry in our country, and they further inquired about how many national banks there were, how much national bank capital there was, how much national bank deposits, loans, and issues there were, and so on. This office felt it difficult to respond and dared not use incomplete and unverified figures to prevaricate. Because we were urged by these questions at the time, we felt that the compilation of the Banking Yearbook could not be delayed any longer, so in June 1933, we formulated the following standards and actively worked:

1. Strive to be suitable for practical use in all aspects.

2. Strive for the most detailed, accurate, and complete records and figures.

3. Set the publication date for June 1934.

From the day the work started to the time the first batch of manuscripts was printed, the time was less than eight months. The compilation method was discussed dozens of times, and more than 10,000 investigation documents were completed to reach the current content. It was due to the concerted efforts of the industry and the assistance of the branches of this bank that the specified standards were not exceeded. Chapters 2, 3, 9, and 11 of this yearbook are the result of directly soliciting completed survey forms from various banks. The forms issued were recognized and assisted by various banks, and they were quickly filled in and returned. If there were any questions, they were also explained in detail, which the editors are very grateful for. Furthermore, the financial institutions in various places must be directly surveyed every year. If personnel are sent for on-site surveys, it is really not allowed due to economic and time constraints. Fortunately, the branches of this bank are all over the provinces, so we used the original communication network of the branches in various places to conduct direct surveys. Chapters 5, 10, and 15 of this yearbook are the result of the efforts of the branches, which are also deeply appreciated by this office. However, due to the short time, the staff members were busy with affairs, and the compilation methods were not good, the statistics were not prepared, the proofreading was not thorough, and the material was not properly selected. It is unavoidable, and everything depends on the readers' corrections and supervision in order to supplement it year by year and reach a state of perfection. This is what the staff of this office especially looks forward to, etc.

Zhou Juemin Invented, the Water Safety Belt Trial Was Successful, All Sectors Considered it Satisfactory After the Trial in Gaoqiao Yesterday 147

The water safety belt invented by Mr. Zhou Juemin of the Shanghai Qunyi Gongji Science Society has now been successfully manufactured. A public trial was held at the Gaoqiao Seaside Bathing Beach in Pudong at 5 pm yesterday, and the results were good. The details are recorded below:

Successful Creation 148

This water safety belt is the only invention of Mr. Zhou's life. After many years of research, he finally succeeded. Its shape is similar to that of a life buoy, but there is a protruding part for storing medicine. One end uses a rubber tube to hold medicine powder. It has been reviewed and approved by the Ministry of Industry and has been registered as a patent.

Instructions for Use 149

This belt is shaped like a vest. Put your head into the hole, and tie the lower belt tightly behind your back. You can quickly crush the medicine pack in the back of the vest to mix it. Then, bravely jump into the water to make the entire vest wet. At this time, the medicine in the vest will suddenly vaporize. Within five or six seconds, the whole body will immediately float to the surface of the water. The entire vest will inflate, keeping you safely afloat. Use your feet to propel yourself towards the shore to wait for rescue. If you are far from the shore and there is no one to rescue you, and you stay in the water for a long time, gradually feeling that the air in the vest is insufficient and the buoyancy is decreasing, you can take the rubber tube on the vest, put it in your mouth, pinch the spring clip with one hand, loosen the rubber tube, and blow air into it to replenish it. After the air is full, release your hand, and the rubber tube will still be clamped, preventing air from leaking. Continue to do this, and you will never sink, waiting for rescue. It is indeed the only preventive device on the water.

Yesterday's Test 150

Yesterday at 5:00 PM, a test was held at the Gaoqiao seaside bathing beach. News media and people from all walks of life were invited in advance, so many people arrived at the time. First, the testers Yu Binqi, Cai Shengmiao, Zhang Bin, Yang Hanzhi, Wang Fubin, Wu Wenhao, Wang Feilong, Xu Zhongqiang, Xu (photographed by Gong Shugui of the Asia East Agency)

Zhongzhi, Yang Jisi, Shi Guiying, Shi Genfu, Shi Changgen, and more than ten others took the belts into the water, crushed the powder, and soon all floated on the surface of the water, remaining unchanged for a long time. Those who saw it were amazed. The test was completed at 6:00 PM. Mr. Zhou plans to widely market it to all sectors of society and win glory for national products.

Intermodal Transport Between Ningbo, Shanghai and Chuanshan to Start on the 12th of this Month, Starting with Passengers 151

The Ningbo-Chuanshan highway has been built, and long-distance buses are already running. To facilitate the round trip of passengers between Shanghai and Chuanshan, the bus company has sent representatives to Shanghai to discuss with the Ningbo-Shaoxing Merchants Shipping Bureau the establishment of an intermodal transport plan. A contract has been signed and is about to be implemented. The general situation is as follows:

Issuing Through Tickets: The Shanghai-Ningbo-Chuanshan intermodal transport is limited to passengers and luggage traveling to and from these three ports. In Shanghai, the Xin Ning Shao Xing and Xin Jiang Tian steamships have been designated as the transport vessels for intermodal transport. Through tickets will be sold by the Merchants Shipping Ningbo-Shaoxing Shipping Bureau on behalf of the bus company, and by the road bureau on behalf of the company in Chuanshan. Detailed rules have also been established for the consignment of passenger luggage to ensure that travelers have no trouble and enjoy various conveniences.

Free Pick-up: Regardless of whether passengers are traveling from Shanghai to Chuanshan or from Chuanshan to Ningbo and then to Shanghai, the long-distance bus company will send special small steamships to pick up passengers at the Xin Jiang Tian and Xin Ning Shao Xing wharves. All those with through tickets are entitled to free rides on the small steamships. Special commissioners will be assigned to transport luggage on behalf of passengers.

Soon to be Implemented: This plan has been agreed upon by both parties and will be implemented starting on the 12th of this month. The Ningbo-Chuanshan Long-Distance Bus Company has sent the proposed plan to the Shanghai Shipping Company. Once it is approved, a public announcement will be made in the newspapers in Shanghai and Ningbo to inform passengers in Shanghai, Ningbo, and Chuanshan.

The Gonghe Steamship of the Public and Harmony Company Experienced a Mishap; Fire Extinguished After Reaching Shanghai Yesterday; Loss of Goods to be Inspected Today 152

The Gonghe steamship of the British Jardine Matheson & Co.'s Yangtze River Line, which was sailing from Hankou to Shanghai, experienced a fire in the rear cargo hold on the afternoon of the 7th while sailing on the Yangtze River near Qixia Mountain upstream of Zhenjiang. Smoke was seen coming out of the cargo hold, and the crew immediately reported it to the ship's owner, who immediately ordered the hatch door to be sealed to prevent ventilation and avoid major danger. At the same time, the ship's personnel were ordered to do their best to extinguish the fire in the cargo hold, and the passengers on board were reassured.

Departed from Zhenjiang for Shanghai: When the ship arrived in Zhenjiang, it stopped as usual to load cargo. The cargo hold where the fire broke out had been sealed and suppressed with inert gas so that it could rush to Shanghai to open the hold for rescue. Some of the passengers on board had disembarked in Zhenjiang, and some had changed to trains to come to Shanghai. After the Gonghe steamship finished loading and unloading in Zhenjiang, it immediately set sail downstream to Shanghai at full speed. At the same time, the ship's owner telegraphed the Shanghai office to prepare fire-fighting boats to open the hold and spray water to extinguish the fire when the ship arrived in Shanghai.

Rescue in Donggou: After the ship rushed back to Shanghai yesterday morning, it berthed in Donggou (opposite the Guanghua Petroleum Company wharf). The Shanghai head office had informed the Fire Brigade, which dispatched two fire boats to Donggou Xiaosha to spray water to extinguish the fire on the Gonghe steamship. Firefighters from the two boats boarded the ship and opened the hatch boards where the fire broke out to fight the fire. From morning to 5:00 PM, the fire was finally extinguished. In addition to being burned, the goods loaded in the cargo hold were also soaked in water, resulting in heavy losses. Fortunately, the other cargo holds were separated, so the impact was minimal.

Inspection Today: At 6:00 PM yesterday, Jardine Matheson & Co. dispatched a small boat to Donggou to tow the Gonghe steamship back to Hongkou and moor it at the Gonghexiang wharf because the fire had been extinguished. All the goods burned by the fire and the water-soaked goods will have to be unloaded today and inspected by a surveyor to determine the losses before handling matters such as water damage assessment. Whether the ship's hull was damaged and how the fire started still needs to be investigated.

Jianghai Customs Seized Smuggled Goods; Crew Members Were All Japanese and Taiwanese 153

Jianghai Customs recently seized two diesel engine vessels similar to fishing boats in the Huangpu River. One was loaded with 400 bales of artificial silk, and the other was loaded with 100 bales of artificial silk and a large amount of flour and sugar, etc. The value is probably over 500,000 yuan. They attempted to evade taxes. The crew members were all Japanese and Taiwanese. Jianghai Customs has confiscated the smuggled goods and the two motor vessels, and the crew members have been released. It is said that the customs plans to auction the confiscated motor vessels.

Continental News reports: On June 29th and 30th, the customs patrol vessel Lianxing seized two Japanese motor fishing boats smuggling goods outside Wusongkou. The amount of smuggled goods seized was unprecedented in recent customs history, including 500 bales of artificial silk worth more than 500,000 yuan, as well as a large amount of flour and sugar. It is said that all have been confiscated. The two fishing boats are equipped with large diesel engines and have been escorted to Shanghai. They were initially moored near the Pudong Water Police Station and then moved to the riverside near Weituoma in Shanghai, guarded by personnel from the Chinese Water Police Bureau. One of the fishing boats carries Japanese crew members and Taiwanese laborers, none of whom carry any passport documents. The two ships have the same structure and are equipped with oil engines, estimated to have a speed of more than 15 nautical miles per hour. The artificial silk carried is clearly intended to be smuggled into Shanghai and is now being unloaded from the ships, one carrying 400 bales and the other carrying 100 bales. It is still unclear whether the two ships sailed from Dalian or Taiwan yesterday. However, it is heard that after the people on board were taken ashore, they were all released because the smuggling of silk goods can only result in the confiscation of the goods or ships, or the imposition of fines, unlike the smuggling of opium and other items, which can lead to imprisonment. Therefore, there is no legal basis to punish the crew members of these two ships. It is now believed that the two ships departed from Dalian, costing around 8,000 to 10,000 taels each. They will probably all be auctioned by the customs for people to bid on.

Happiness Turns to Sorrow: Zhang Wensheng Dies from Exhaustion; Lover Flees in Fear; Illegal Hotel Under Investigation 154

Zhang Wensheng, a 45-year-old man from Dongtai, Jiangbei, residing at No. 56, 40 Jiantou, Rue du Pere Froc, French Concession, was tall and obese. He worked as a servant in a mansion. He had a wife, Ms. Chen, 38 years old, a son and two daughters, and an elderly mother at home. However, Zhang still had a strong liking for women and often frequented brothels. Yesterday morning around 8:00 AM, Zhang met his lover, Ms. Zhang, 26 years old, near the Xiaocai Market in Baxianqiao. She was carrying a basket and scales to buy vegetables at the market. Upon seeing her, Zhang took her to the Yuandan Inn at No. 13 Huagequan Road, where he used the alias Wang Ar'er, 38 years old, from Zhenjiang. Upon entering the inn, without paying the room fee, he took the woman upstairs and ordered the tea boy to open room number two. They then closed the door to engage in intercourse. Unexpectedly, during this hot weather, Zhang, due to physical weakness and exhaustion, opened his essence gate and spilled all over the bed. Ms. Zhang was anxious and feared that making a fuss would be detrimental to her. She put on her clothes, took the vegetable basket and scales she brought, and pretended to be calm as she went downstairs, claiming that she was in a hurry to buy vegetables and fled. The tea boy waited downstairs for several minutes and did not see Zhang come down. He went upstairs to check and collect the room fee. The tea boy, Wu Axin, entered the room and saw Zhang lying on the bed, frothing at the mouth. When asked, he could not open his mouth to answer and was already on his last breath. The tea boy was greatly shocked and mistakenly thought that he was suffering from acute cholera. He informed the innkeeper and hired a rickshaw to send Zhang to the Shanghai Epidemic Hospital on Xizang Road for treatment. After the doctor examined him, he was diagnosed with exhaustion and no pulse and refused to admit him. Zhang, while sitting in the rickshaw, also died at that moment. The tea boy and others who accompanied him planned to send the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Hall for a post-mortem examination and requested acceptance before reporting to the police. On the way, it was discovered by Chinese Constable No. 574 and taken to the Meilan Police Station at the Grand Clock. Detectives were sent to carry the body into the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Hall for a post-mortem examination and to summon the family to the case. The court was requested to send someone to examine the body today. It is heard that the police are investigating the owner and tea boy of the Yuandan Inn for allowing prostitution during the day, which violates the regulations, and have summoned them to the case for interrogation.

Trial of the Service Staff Fraud Case at the Sixth District Third Branch; Extorting 210 Yuan for Investigating Opium; Witnesses Testify in Court About the Incident 155

Mei Liujiang, a villager from Meilong Town in the suburbs of Shanghai, used to be in the rice business. In recent years, due to his old age, he has been unemployed at home. He has a habit of smoking opium. He spends his free time lying on a couch at home. This was discovered by Liu Yin, a service staff member from the police station of the Sixth District Third Branch in the town. On May 28th, he led the police to Mei Liujiang's house, claiming to search for prohibited items such as red pills and morphine. As a result, nothing was found. Afterwards, the town spread rumors that the service staff member was engaged in fraud, and the local people submitted a complaint to the Municipal Public Security Bureau, accusing Liu Yin of illegal activities and extortion. After receiving the report, Director Wen believed that the matter concerned the reputation of the police and that the truth should be thoroughly investigated. He summoned Liu Yin to the case and sent a letter to the prosecutor's office of the local court for investigation. Prosecutor Lei interrogated him and ordered him to be detained, and also summoned Mei Liujiang and others.

Repeated Investigations 156

Mei Liujiang was released on bail, and the case was prosecuted in the criminal court for public trial. The previous morning, Judge Sun Jikang held an open trial in the Fifth Court and ordered the detained Liu Yin to be brought to the case. Liu Yin confessed that he was a service staff member at the Meilong Town Police Station of the Sixth District Third Branch. On May 26th, he was ordered to go to Mei Liujiang's house to search for drugs such as red pills and morphine. At that time, he led police officers Zhao Bingwen, Luo Ren, and Li Shuangying to search, but no prohibited items were found, nor was there any extortion. Zhao Bingwen then testified that he was a police chief at the Meilong Town Police Station. On that day, he was ordered by the service staff member to lead Luo and Li to Mei Liujiang's house to search. Service staff member Liu ordered me to go and call Mei Jinchun and Mei Hongyuan to go to Mei Liujiang's house together. When I went to call them and arrived at the entrance of Mei Liujiang's house, I only saw many people.

Crowded at the Entrance 157

So I did not go in. Not long after, the service staff member came out, having found nothing, and returned to the station. Mei Liujiang testified that he was 63 years old, from Shanghai, and lived in Meilong Town. He had a son and a daughter. He used to be in the rice business, but now he is old and sick. He does not deny smoking opium, but he only smokes a few times a month when he is ill, and he has not smoked for more than a month now. (Question) Did the police find anything during the search? (Answer) What they found was an opium pipe, a jar of ashes, and five opium stems. (Question) What day was that? (Answer) In the afternoon of May 28th, four people came and said they were investigating the household registration. After they found the opium paraphernalia, they said that this was a prohibited item and wanted to take me away. Later, Mei Jinchun acted as a guarantor. At that time, they did not say they wanted money. At 8:00 PM that night, Liu Yin came and said that Director Wu Zhengding wanted to fine you 400 yuan. I replied that I had no money. He said that if I did not have a penny, the whole family would be taken away. Later, my wife said that she would take out some money. I agreed to pay 40 yuan, but he did not agree. Then he added to it,

Two Pudong Newspapers Sued; The Xin Pudong Bao and the Pudong Xing Bao Cause a Disturbance for Publishing a Gambling Case in Zhoupu 162

The Xin Pudong Bao has been published for many years and is known for its fair opinions. It is particularly sensitive and accurate in reporting news from villages and towns in Pudong. However, it has always criticized and condemned不良 events such as opium and gambling in rural areas, without any favoritism. A Tongxing Clothing Store in Zhoupu, due to its sluggish business and high expenses, opened a secret gambling den in its store as another way to make money to make up for the losses. It attracted gamblers and opened the den after closing the market every yesterday. The winnings and losses were huge, and the store enjoyed the benefits of collecting commissions. As time went on, it gradually leaked out. The Xin Pudong Bao revealed its secret on May 27th, publishing a news story about the store opening a gambling den and collecting commissions, with the headline "Gambling Den Set Up Inside Tongxing Clothing Store". However, the store owner Ni Qiusheng insisted on denying it and sent a letter to the newspaper requesting a correction. However, the newspaper believed that the report was indeed a fact and refused his request. It continued to publish the inside story of the gambling den, stating that a gambler surnamed Shen was playing mahjong in the gambling den one day and drew a set of three yuan cards. Among them, the white board had already been "ponged" out. Er'er (named Zhang Aichun, the owner of the local Gongheyuan Restaurant), who was watching, suddenly said, "This set of cards may not be able to win." Shen believed that this remark was tantamount to giving a warning, so after the game ended, he hosted a banquet for people from all walks of life in Zhoupu and announced the inside story of the clothing store setting up a gambling den to collect money on the spot. He also implicated Jin Dongsheng of the Delongmao Meat Shop and Qiu Jinsheng of the Zhoupu Watermelon Shop. The Pudong Xing Bao also published a news story titled "Gambling Case in Zhoupu" on May 28th. Ni, Zhang, Jin, and Qiu hired lawyers to file criminal self-suits against the chief writers of the two newspapers, Qu Wuyong and Tang Mengwu, in the First Special District Local Court. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhan summoned them for interrogation. Tang Mengwu did not appear, but Qu Wuyong surrendered himself and stated that the Xin Pudong Bao had another person in charge and that he only occasionally wrote commentaries. Moreover, the newspaper was not for sale and its reports were always very cautious, etc. The court then decided to postpone the hearing.

Shashi Steamship Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday; Ship Owner Reports Details of Accident 163

The Shashi steamship of the British Swire Group's Shanghai-Changsha line arrived at a river section near Changsha on the 3rd of this month when the cotton yarn and cloth stored in the cargo hold suddenly caught fire. Fortunately, the ship's fire-fighting equipment was complete and was quickly extinguished. The water-damaged goods were unloaded in Changsha. The ship's hull was undamaged and continued to sail to Shanghai as usual. It arrived in Shanghai at 11:00 AM yesterday and berthed at the company's wharf in Pudong. The ship owner reported the details of the accident to the company's manager in Shanghai. Although it was quickly extinguished, many of the goods were water-damaged, resulting in heavy losses. After the goods are unloaded, it is scheduled to sail from Shanghai to Changsha as usual on the 10th.

End of the Gao Tao Case: Gao Granted Probation After Appeal for Assault 170

Gao Xiaochen (named Quanzhong), formerly the garrison commander of Xiamen and a native of Xuzhou, and Tao Jiayao, formerly the governor of Jiangxi Province and a native of Gan, had a debt dispute in Japan concerning the late Xu Guoliang, former head of the Shanghai Municipal Police. Gao hired a lawyer and filed a criminal lawsuit against Tao in the Special No. 2 Court, accusing him of fraud. Tao, feeling aggrieved by the sudden accusation despite having cleared the matter, filed a countersuit accusing Gao of false accusation.

While the countersuit was being heard, Gao, enraged by Tao's insulting remarks in court, assaulted Tao on the stairs inside the courthouse after the adjournment, causing him to vomit blood. Tao then filed an assault charge against Gao. After trial, Gao was sentenced to six months in prison for assault. Later, through mediation by friends, Tao compensated Gao 4,000 yuan, and Gao withdrew his lawsuit, settling the matter, as reported in previous issues. However, Gao, dissatisfied with the original sentence in Tao's assault case against him, hired lawyers Xiang Xun and Liu Cailiang to file an appeal with the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. The Third Branch, after summoning witnesses and holding a court hearing, concluded that the evidence of the appellant's assault was conclusive. The court announced its verdict the day before yesterday, rejecting Gao Xiaochen's appeal and granting him a two-year suspended sentence. Thus, this high-profile case of a garrison commander assaulting a provincial governor and their mutual accusations came to an end.

Publication of the New-Style Punctuated "Easy Guide to Ma's Grammar"

Letter to the Editor 178

Dear Editor,

On July 7th, I read in the "Local News" section of your newspaper that the 15th meeting of the Ship Collision Handling Dispute Committee of the Shanghai Navigation Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, chaired by Penghu, continued to discuss the case of the Yuxing Wheel colliding with and sinking the Shao Genggen civilian boat in the Huangpu River. The meeting questioned Tang Yinguo, the deputy of the Longmao small wheel, and Ling Zhaoji, the captain of the Yuxing Wheel, and (resolved) that the Shao Genggen civilian boat should bear 60% of the responsibility for the negligence, and the Yuxing Wheel should bear 40% of the responsibility for the negligence.

After reading this, I was very surprised. The case of Shao Genggen's rice boat being hit and sunk by the Yuxing Wheel in the Huangpu River around 2:00 PM on May 7th, and his wife Shao Guizhen tragically drowning and dying, has been inspected and verified by the Shanghai Local Court, and after questioning and investigation, it was deemed that a public prosecution should be filed and transferred to the Criminal Court for public judgment. We should wait quietly for the judgment according to law. As for the private claim for damages, it has already been entrusted to my lawyer, Te Quan, to act as an agent, requesting a judgment for payment.

On June 16th, Shao Genggen again commissioned my lawyer to publish a notice in the Shen and Xin newspapers, stating that the signature was invalid, denying mediation as uneasy, and advocating for a solution according to law. The Shanghai Navigation Administration Bureau's Ship Collision Handling Dispute Committee had previously unreasonably requested twice to publish a correction in the newspaper. My lawyer only knows to speak law in law, and knows nothing else, so he once replied and did not allow it. Your newspaper's "Local News" section yesterday (July 7th) reported the situation of the 15th meeting of the Ship Collision Committee, knowing that the committee failed to thoroughly investigate the facts of the case and its course of events, and used the partial statements of Tang, the deputy of the Longmao small wheel related to the Xingyu Wheel, and Ling Zhaoji, the captain of the Xingyu Wheel, as the standard for the committee's resolution. This is a lack of fairness in the meeting system, and it is clear that the decision was made with suspicion, intending to involve the legal effect.

In addition to presenting the facts of the case to the Control Yuan and the Ministry of Communications for investigation and handling according to law, in order to emphasize civil life, I will again request your newspaper to publish the original letter in the "Letters to the Editor" column, in order to correct the truth of the case and avoid confusing the facts, I am deeply grateful.

Dear Editor,

My client, Jia Li, took her two nieces from Xinzha Road to Dongxinqiao by the No. 3 tram around 8:00 AM on the 7th of this month. When they arrived at Dongxinqiao Station, the ticket seller and driver saw that she was a woman, poor and weak, and urged her to leave quickly. Ms. Jia was unable to resist, so she and her nieces got off the bus. One of the nieces, Li Fengfu (also known as Hongfu), was only four years old, and the other was only eight months old and still in swaddling clothes. At this time, the older child got off first, and just as she landed, the ticket seller rang the bell, and the driver, seeing that Ms. Jia and her nieces had not completely got off the bus, hurriedly turned the wheel, causing a tragedy. She died of her injuries around 6:00 PM on the afternoon of the same day.

July 8th

Reading Q&A

Relative Truth and Absolute Truth - Answer to Messrs. Tian Zhao, Yin Jishan, et al. - (Continued) 179

Even the simplest truth, like death, may seem self-evident to us. However, primitive hunting societies, due to limitations in their social practices, may not have a complete understanding of it. Therefore, more complex and profound truths are even more subject to practical limitations. Relative truth is a necessary stage in the process of people approaching absolute truth. Each relative truth is only a part of absolute truth. Absolute truth is multifaceted, while relative truth is one aspect of it. Human understanding gradually approaches absolute truth through the process of relative truth. Therefore, understanding is also a kind of movement. Truth is not fixed in human minds. The things reflected in truth gradually unfold like an active film. Each frame represents a part of the entire movie, and the entire movie is composed of these many parts. Therefore, absolute truth is the sum, total, or conclusion of relative truths.

In this way, we can know that there is an inseparable relationship between relative truth and absolute truth. Without relative truth, absolute truth cannot be reached. Without absolute truth, relative truth has no conclusion. Old philosophy, especially idealistic philosophy, completely denied relative truth when advocating absolute truth, believing that absolute truth could be reached suddenly, without having to gradually understand it through practice. However, once separated from practice, one cannot help but replace the truth of reality with fantasy, resulting in dogmatism and idealism, which is wrong. As for those who advocate relative truth, they only pay attention to immediate empirical evidence and do not believe that truth can be used to infer future things. They only pay attention to the present and do not trust future results, which will lead to skepticism. However, in fact, truth can predict the future. A truth in science will never deceive us. Those who advocate only relative truth, in fact, ignore the value of science, which we naturally want to oppose.

It should also be pointed out that relative truth has the possibility of developing into absolute truth, as has been said before. And absolute truth itself is by no means completely fixed. Once the things we understand increase, we can make the absolute truth we have reached richer and more concrete, making it a higher absolute truth. The universe is infinitely diverse in all aspects, and the development of truth is also infinite. Compared with the infinitely diverse universe, the absolute truth we have reached is still a relative and incomplete thing. It only has absolute and complete meaning in a certain stage of our practice. The more practice develops, the richer the content of absolute truth will be, and the higher the value of its truth will be.

Ministry of Finance to Order All Provinces and Cities to Establish Schools to Train Tax Officials 181

To Cultivate Basic Talents and Thoroughly Reform Finance

Students Admitted Must Have Graduated from Junior High School

In order to create basic talents for financial administration personnel and thoroughly reform finance, the Ministry of Finance initiated the establishment of schools in various provinces and cities to train basic financial talents. The method has now been finalized and can be ordered to the financial bureaus of various provinces to follow. The reporter from the Daily News found out the details of the implementation of the school's establishment and has recorded them as follows:

Establishing Schools 182

The Ministry of Finance believes that the improvement of finance lies in the goodness of legislation, and even more in the strength of its implementation. However, due to the changes in social economy and the adoption of new budget laws, the old-fashioned money and grain practices are no longer suitable. There is a great lack of newly arrived talents. In recent years, the authorities of various provinces have either used examinations to select true talents or established schools to train them. However, their purpose is mostly for middle-level and above financial personnel, and there are no examinations or training for lower-level personnel. As a result, matters such as investigation, collection, and disbursement of finance in various counties are still controlled by the old-fashioned clerks. Government measures are sometimes delayed under the pretext of training, not implemented, or superficially complied with, temporarily decorated. In severe cases, they hinder the officials and obstruct the new mechanism. The failure to thoroughly clean up the finance is really one of the reasons. Now, the finances of various provinces and cities are striving for clarification. If the management of books, the collection of taxes, and the compilation of accounting statistics are not changed to be handled by specially trained and qualified personnel, but are still entrusted to the old-fashioned clerks who are unlearned and unprincipled, it will be difficult to achieve good results. In order to thoroughly reform finance, it is urgent to train these lower-level financial personnel to meet the current needs of reform.

Proposed Methods 183

(1) The financial bureaus of various provinces and cities should establish schools to train basic financial talents as soon as possible. In order to save expenses, they may encourage groups or private individuals to establish schools, provide them with convenience, and help them develop. (2) The student admission qualifications for this type of school should be limited to junior high school graduates, or those with equivalent qualifications, or those who have served in society for a certain number of years. (3) The curriculum should be practical, such as financial laws and regulations, tax laws and regulations, accounting and statistical laws and regulations, and the financial and economic situation of the province, all of which should be taken as important subjects. (4) Moral education should focus on cultivating civic morality, developing labor habits, and inspiring a spirit of service, so as to improve their skills and enhance their personality. (5) After graduation, students should be screened and employed by the financial bureau. All agencies in the province and city that need tax collectors, accountants, statisticians, etc., should designate and assign them from the previously trained and qualified personnel.

Results of the Zhejiang High School Graduation Examination Announced 184

The results of the Zhejiang Province High School Graduation Examination for this year have been reviewed by the examination committee members. According to the score calculation results, 252 students passed all subjects and are allowed to graduate, including 12 students with a grade of A, 181 students with a grade of B, and 59 students with a grade of C. 89 students failed one or two subjects and are allowed to participate in the next examination for those subjects. 30 students failed three or more subjects and are required to repeat the grade and participate in the examination. 5 students who failed to complete three or more subjects due to illness or other reasons should participate in the full examination in the next session. 6 students who failed the school graduation examination should send the make-up exam results for review. In addition, 4 students who participated in this year's examination and passed the make-up examination for the second and third graduation examinations are allowed to graduate. The first place in the individual category is Jiang Yimei from Ningbo Middle School, and the first place in the group category is Ningbo Xiaoshi Middle School.

The Committee for the Examination of Books and Magazines Hosted the Publishing Industry Yesterday, Announcing the Revised Examination Methods 185

The Committee for the Examination of Books and Magazines of the Central Propaganda Committee has been established in Shanghai for a month. In order to make the publishing industry understand the significance of the central government's establishment of this committee, the committee hosted a tea party for the publishing industry at Yipinxian Hall at 4:00 PM yesterday. Zhang Guangyu, Fu Donghua, Ma Guoliang, Liang Desuo, Zhang Yiping, Du Chongyuan, Xia Mianzun, Yao Mingda, Chen Lin, Zhao Jingshen, Li Bojia, Lou Pengnian, Li Zhiyun, Zhang Jinglu, Xu Yuyuan, Fang Dongliang, Wang Zicheng, Wang Yuanfang, Zhao Nangong, Yu Songhua, Gao Pengtian, Ji Zhizhong, Shen Junsheng, Wu Liande, Zheng Wuchang, Sun Shimin and other responsible persons of various bookstores and social organizations attended, totaling more than 50 people. Fang Zhi (Secretary of the Central Propaganda Committee), Li Songfeng (Director of the Police Department of the Ministry of Interior), Pan Gongzhan (Director of the Municipal Education Bureau), and members Sun Dezhong, Xiang Deyan, etc. reported on the organization and operation of the committee. The details are described as follows:

Chairman Fang Zhi Reported 186

First, Fang Zhi reported, saying, "I am very grateful for your presence at the reception today. There are many books and magazines published in Shanghai, and the authors are also gathered in Shanghai. Therefore, Shanghai is the cultural center of the country. The publishing industry's efforts to improve culture will be assisted by the authorities. However, the authorities must impose penalties on the improper books in accordance with the law. However, the publishing industry has repeatedly requested to find a way to remedy the great loss caused by deletions, revisions, or detentions after distribution. After repeated consideration, the deletion, revision, or detention loss is quite large. Therefore, the committee organized this association in Shanghai to conduct preliminary review of manuscripts, so as to avoid losses such as detention and prohibition after publication. The committee will review the manuscripts submitted to the committee quickly and will not delay the publication time. Although the committee is located in Shanghai, it is actually a central government agency. This point should also be explained to you."

Li Songfeng and Others' Report 187

Li Songfeng then reported, roughly stating that according to the detailed rules for the implementation of the Publication Law, the review of original manuscripts should have been carried out long ago. Now, all the methods of the committee established by the central government are based on the Publication Law and the detailed rules for its implementation. He hoped that in the future, the publishing industry would, in accordance with the law, submit original manuscripts of literary, artistic, and social science books and periodicals to the committee for review. Pan Gongzhan reported, roughly stating that since the establishment of the committee, many parties have submitted manuscripts for review in accordance with the law, but there are still some who have not. He attributed the reasons to two points: first, some people are still unaware of this matter due to the transfer of official documents; second, some are taking a wait-and-see attitude. The committee has now revised the review methods and hopes that the publishing industry can cooperate effectively with the committee. If submissions are not made in the future, penalties will be imposed in accordance with the law. Sun Dezhong and Xiang Deyan reported, roughly stating that the central government's requirement for the review of publications is for the sake of the nation's future and social thought. They hoped that writers and the publishing industry would, from this standpoint, cooperate effectively with the committee and pay attention to the matter. Furthermore, indicating the review certificate number on the books could reduce delays for the publishing industry. Finally, several representatives of the publishing industry expressed that the publishing industry felt very convenient about the central government's establishment of the committee and the speed of its review of manuscripts. Finally, the chairman announced that the committee's address has now been moved to Yishiyuan Garden, at the end of Shangwen Road, South City, also known as Ninghe Road. The telephone numbers borrowed from the Chinese district are 22401 and 22402.

Revised Review Methods 188

(Article 1) These methods are formulated in accordance with Article 5 of the Organizational Regulations of the Book and Magazine Review Committee of the Central Propaganda Committee and the provisions of the detailed rules for the implementation of the Publication Law. (Article 2) All books and magazines published by bookstores, social organizations, or authors within the Republic of China should, in accordance with these methods, submit the manuscript to the Book and Magazine Review Committee of the Central Propaganda Committee (hereinafter referred to as "the Committee") for review before printing. The aforementioned review matters shall be carried out in accordance with the resolutions of the 115th Standing Committee Meeting of the Central Executive Committee: (1) The scope of review is literature, art, and social sciences; (2) The pilot program will first be conducted in Shanghai. (Article 3) When submitting a manuscript of a book or magazine for review, the applicant shall provide the following information: A. Title of the book or periodical; B. Number of pages of the manuscript and its attachments; C. Name and address of the applicant; D. Name and address of the author or editor. (Article 4) The Committee shall provide all submitted book and magazine manuscripts with the convenience of prompt review. (Article 5) Those who meet any of the following conditions may submit a request to the Committee to forward to the Central Propaganda Committee for approval and issuance of a review exemption certificate. The application form for requesting review exemption shall be determined separately: 1. Books and magazines published by local party and government organs; 2. Magazines that have been published for more than one year and whose ideas have always been correct and have never violated the standards for the review of propaganda materials and the Publication Law promulgated by the central government. If any inappropriate content is found in the aforementioned books and magazines granted review exemption, in addition to revoking the review exemption certificate, penalties shall be imposed in accordance with the law. (Article 6) Those who have not been granted review exemption and do not submit the manuscript for review shall be punished in accordance with the provisions of Article 11 of the detailed rules for the implementation of the Publication Law. (Article 7) If the content of a book or magazine manuscript submitted for review is deemed inappropriate, it may be returned to the original applicant with instructions to revise it in accordance with the review comments. If the entire text violates the provisions of Article 3 of the standards for the review of propaganda materials and the restrictions of Article 19 of Chapter 4 of the Publication Law, the Committee may withhold the original copy and submit it to the Central Propaganda Committee for verification and handling. (Article 8) The Committee shall issue a review certificate for book and magazine manuscripts that have been reviewed and approved by the Committee. (Article 9) All book and magazine manuscripts that have obtained a review certificate or review exemption certificate shall have the review certificate or review exemption certificate number printed on the cover or bottom page for identification when published. (Article 10) The Committee shall submit book and periodical manuscripts that are deemed to warrant punishment to the Central Propaganda Committee for verification and handling. (Article 11) After the publication of books and magazines, in addition to sending two copies of each type to the Ministry of Interior in accordance with the provisions of Articles 13 and 15 of the Publication Law, three copies should also be sent to the Committee for verification and filing. If any discrepancies are found between the published version and the reviewed manuscript after the publication of books and magazines, the Committee shall request the Central Propaganda Committee to forward them to the Ministry of Interior for punishment. (Article 12) The Committee shall list and submit books and magazines that have been reviewed and approved by the Committee to the Central Propaganda Committee for forwarding to the Ministry of Interior for record. (Article 13) If there are any matters not covered in these methods, the Committee may request the Central Propaganda Committee to revise them. (Article 14) These methods shall be promulgated and implemented by the Central Propaganda Committee.

Key Points for Improvement in Vocational Education in Jiangsu Province 189

Report by an Inspector of the Ministry of Education

The Ministry of Education recently dispatched Inspector Zhong Daozan to inspect the state of vocational education in Jiangsu Province. The inspection report has been submitted to the Ministry of Education. The key points regarding the urgent need to improve vocational education in Jiangsu Province are recorded below.

A. General Matters 190

1. Apart from the Provincial Zha She Guan Sericulture Vocational School, there are no other independent institutions for girls' vocational education in the province. One or two more should be added to expand opportunities for girls' vocational education.

2. Provincial schools are mostly of a higher level. Before primary vocational schools can be established everywhere at the local level, they should consider running primary vocational schools concurrently, as appropriate, to meet the needs.

3. Home economics education is rarely promoted in various provinces and cities. The province, as a developed area of education, should vigorously promote it and establish schools to implement it.

4. Many private commercial vocational schools are not true to their name. They have neither commercial practice facilities nor sufficient and appropriate commercial cultivation, and are no different from ordinary middle schools. They should be banned and ordered to be converted into commercial vocational supplementary classes when possible, and to accept young shop assistants and apprentices to facilitate practical application.

5. Middle schools and vocational schools should be set up separately. Do not allow various vocational subjects to continue to be affiliated to middle schools, in order to comply with the regulations.

6. Efforts should be made to promote and reward the development of private vocational schools with good results. However, the establishment of commercial vocational schools should be based on environmental needs and subject to appropriate restrictions.

7. The talents and equipment of existing vocational schools should be used to the fullest extent possible to attach various vocational supplementary schools or classes as needed.

8. It has been found that the physical education regulations for vocational schools stipulate 20 minutes per day, which should be carried out within the practical work time to balance students' physical and mental health. All schools have failed to comply, and attention should be paid to this.

9. The names of the original vocational schools should be corrected immediately in accordance with the regulations, in order to standardize them.

B. Matters Concerning Various Schools 191

1. The facilities of the Provincial Yixing Agricultural School have been inadequate in the past, and the training and practical work of students are particularly lax. Agricultural and forestry tools and reference books are also very lacking. Improvements and enrichment are urgently needed.

2. The Provincial Yixing Pottery School has 20 students and an annual fee of 20,000 yuan, which is uneconomical. The school plans to add a senior high school class to manufacture ceramic tiles, but according to past experience, enrollment is not easy, and it is even more difficult to enroll junior high school students. It can be changed to enroll senior elementary school students for a five-year graduation. At the same time, supplementary classes can be added to enroll factory apprentices. The pricing of the school's products is too high, making it difficult to sell. The pottery carving and other subjects only have one or two hours per week, which should be appropriately increased. Methods and techniques such as color mixing and flower matching, and identification of flame colors should be added, and students should be proficient and clear. They should also actively conduct research with local businesses to improve the pottery industry.

3. The Provincial Suqian Glass Vocational School has been operating for a short time and has achieved good results. However, most of its products are cups, plates, oil lamps, and lampshades, which compete with existing products on the market. It should also manufacture all the glass equipment needed for physics, chemistry, and biology to resist a portion of foreign goods. The classes should not be limited to senior levels. For products, attention should be paid to the research of heat resistance.

4. The Provincial Huaiyin Agricultural School has more than 40 faculty and staff, including 17 full-time teachers, 9 part-time teachers, 17 staff members, and 20 school workers. It is said that it is difficult to reduce the number due to the environment and scattered school buildings. Judging from the number of classes and students, there are too many. Efforts should be made to reduce the number, and the manufacturing of agricultural products needs to be improved.

5. The Provincial Suzhou Industrial School lacks books, and most of the instruments are outdated. Factory practice in the third grade only accounts for one-quarter of the total time, and even less in the first and second grades. The dyeing and weaving performance is poor. The Department of Education ordered the school to focus on production in the future, but it has not been able to proceed due to lack of capital. More workers should be recruited to assist students in production while implementing vocational supplementary education.

6. The Chemical Engineering Department of the Provincial Suzhou Middle School and the Civil Engineering Department of the Provincial Yangzhou Middle School, both of which are affiliated with senior vocational departments, have achieved considerable results. However, Suzhou Middle School is adjacent to the Provincial Industrial School, and the Chemical Engineering Department should be merged into the Industrial School for dedicated responsibility. The Civil Engineering Department of Yangzhou Middle School should also be merged into the Civil Engineering Department of the Suzhou Industrial School. If it is deemed necessary, a separate school can be set up for the planned water conservancy department to comply with the regulations for the separate establishment of vocational schools.

7. The Provincial Wusong Fisheries School was well-equipped, but suffered heavy losses due to the January 28 Incident in Shanghai. Subsequently, the Department of Education allocated 40,000 yuan, of which 30,000 yuan was used to repair school buildings and 10,000 yuan was used to replenish machinery, which is less than one-sixth of the original equipment. Teaching is difficult. The cannery cannot produce due to incomplete equipment and lack of working capital. Efforts should be made to restore the old appearance as soon as possible. Students lack the habit of hard work and should also pay attention to this.

8. The Provincial Suzhou Agricultural School, in addition to focusing on crop improvement in the horticulture department, should also pay attention to flower and garden design. The agricultural product manufacturing in the agronomy department must add machinery to improve products.

9. The Private Qiming Xiguang Shuxue Chengzhi An Ding Senior and Junior Commercial Vocational Schools, except for Qiming, which originally planned to run a commercial school, the rest are limited to the establishment of senior and junior high schools. They have no choice but to switch to commerce, but in fact they still implement middle school education. A close examination of their class schedules reveals that commercial subjects account for less than one-seventh of the total. As for practice, there is only a dilapidated school store, one or two typewriters, and very little learning time, which is of no practical value. Efforts should be made to ban them and restrict their establishment.

10. The establishment of the Private Nantong College Affiliated Senior Textile Department and Middle School was motivated by the proposal of the Chinese Textile Mill Federation to train intermediate technicians. The Federation was responsible for an annual operating expense of 30,000 yuan, but has only paid for half a year and has not continued to pay. The economy is very tight, the teaching spirit is also poor, and there is no performance to show. The planned metalworking equipment, such as sand casting, models, carpentry, and forging, are all constrained by the economy and cannot be carried out. Efforts should be made to subsidize it. The middle school attached to the agricultural department has no need in the environment and should be converted into senior agronomy and animal husbandry departments to utilize existing equipment and talents to promote them.

11. The Private Zhenjiang Girls' Junior Vocational School's sericulture department has only 9 to 11 hours of vocational subjects per week, and the home economics normal department has only 4 to 6 hours of vocational subjects per week. General subjects, such as Chinese, English, arithmetic, physics, and chemistry, often have as many as 5 to 9 hours, which is largely inconsistent. The home economics normal department lacks equipment, the practice is very insufficient, and the current facilities are not in line with the original purpose of the department. Attention should be paid to home economics labor subjects. It is best to focus entirely on home economics and gardening education for the first three years. Those who aspire to be elementary school labor teachers should extend their studies by one year to specialize in psychology, teaching methods, and teaching material organization.

12. The Private Zhengze Girls' Vocational School's senior painting department has few people and no results to speak of. Applied art courses should be increased, embroidery courses can add sewing subjects, and the three-year rattan work subject should be deleted. The ordinary normal school should be closed or converted into a home economics labor normal department. Supplementary classes are still developed and should be expanded.

13. The Zhenjiang County Vocational Supplementary School and the Nantong County Girls' Vocational Supplementary School, the former has courses in document editing, stabbing, and electroplating, and the latter has courses in sewing and embroidery. Since the purpose of setting up the courses has not been determined, all equipment and teaching are simple and ordinary, and there are no results to speak of. The students in the document course are young and have a low level, and the facilities are particularly inappropriate. They urgently need to be enriched and improved.

14. The Private Southeast Vocational School has agricultural and commercial departments. The commercial department has no equipment. The agricultural field is only five mu. In the first semester, the number of people was sharply reduced because the school was not registered. Parents requested that more general subjects be set up to facilitate further education. In order to adapt to the environment, the school reduced the vocational subjects. The setting of existing subjects is chaotic, without a certain standard. A few school directors are willing to donate farmland and provide strong assistance if the school has a proper reorganization plan. Efforts should be made to assist in the reorganization.

15. The Private Guanghua Junior Simple Chemical Engineering Vocational School has a small and simple practice place, and the planned learning subjects are too complicated, many but not refined. They urgently need to be enriched and improved. Principal Yang Zhengyu also holds a teaching position at a certain university in Shanghai and is not often at school. School affairs are the responsibility of the director of teaching affairs, which is not appropriate.

16. The Private Zhengyi Junior Vocational School originally had commercial and home economics departments, which were not well-managed. After the summer vacation, the commercial department plans to convert to a salt affairs department, focusing on management and manufacturing. It should be converted to senior level and pay attention to curriculum formulation and teacher selection to achieve practical results. The content of the existing home economics curriculum is too simple and not true to its name. Principal Cao Chu is currently the principal of the Provincial Zhenjiang Normal School and only goes to the school once a week, which is inappropriate.

The Municipal Education Bureau, in accordance with the order of the Ministry of Education, has designated National Jiaotong University and Private Datong University to jointly organize the Shanghai Municipal Secondary School Science Teachers' Summer Training Class. Registration time is from 9:00 am to 12:00 noon and from 1:00 pm to 4:00 pm every day, location: National Jiaotong University, Xujiahui, this city. All incumbent or prospective science teachers in public, municipal, registered, and unregistered middle schools in this city should follow the previous order to issue a simple application and register for admission. Otherwise, they will not be allowed to continue or take up the position of science teachers in secondary schools in this city in the next semester. In addition, the committee members, in order to facilitate the study of incumbent science teachers in middle schools outside this city, may also register for admission.

Sports News

Hulbert Den Became a British Triumph; Langrishe Wins Women's Singles Again 207

American Jacobs Suffers Defeat at 1-2

America Wins Men's Doubles Championship

Tournament Concludes with All Titles Decided

(London, 7th, Reuters) Miss Dorothy Langrishe, Britain's top female tennis player, displayed exceptionally beautiful tennis today, defeating the All-American Women's Champion, Miss Helen Jacobs, to win the Hulbert Den Women's Singles Championship. The scores are as follows:

Langrishe (UK) 6-2, 5-7, 6-3, Jacobs (US)

It has been eight years since a British woman won the Hulbert Den Women's Championship, the last time being in 1926. It has been a full twenty-five years since British players simultaneously won the men's and women's titles, the last time being in 1909. Langrishe's victory was a deserved result. From beginning to end, she displayed great confidence, neutralizing the opponent's powerful chops, and her serves and shots were more powerful than usual.

First Set: Jacobs served first and won the first game, but thereafter Langrishe controlled the situation, easily winning the first set with a score of 6-2.

Second Set: Jacobs increased her speed, taking an early lead at 2-1, 3-2, and then 5-3. However, Langrishe retaliated with extremely heavy sideline shots, tying the score at 5-5. At this point, she showed slight nervousness, and Jacobs seized the opportunity to win two consecutive games, taking the second set at 7-5.

Third Set: In the third set, Langrishe regained her confidence, displaying extremely beautiful ball skills, hitting several half-volleys and smashes, and aggressively attacking Jacobs' backhand, winning again at 6-3 and taking the championship.

Men's Doubles Final 208

The result of the Men's Doubles Final: The American championship team of Lott and Stoefen defeated the French duo of Borotra and Brugnon, who had held the championship for two years. The scores are as follows:

Lott and Stoefen (US) 6-2, 6-3, 6-4, Borotra and Brugnon (France). This French team lacked any of its former prowess. The Americans' powerful serves were often deadly, and their pressure was twice as strong as that of the French. (Havas) The American Lott and Stoefen's three consecutive victories over France are attributed to their ability to exploit the opponent's momentum. The French technique was very skillful, but their failure to capitalize on the opponent's momentum led to their defeat.

Women's Doubles Final 209

The result of the Women's Doubles Final: Miss Ryan (US) and Mrs. Mathieu (France) defeated Mrs. Andrews (US) and Mrs. Henrotin (France). The scores are as follows:

Miss Ryan (US) 6-3, Mrs. Andrews (US)

Mrs. Mathieu (France) 6-3, Mrs. Henrotin (France). This was Miss Ryan's twenty-sixth appearance in a Hulbert Den final and her thirteenth victory. Although the level of play today was not up to standard, Ryan was undoubtedly the best of the four. The pairing of an American and a French woman on each side was noteworthy. The King and Queen of England attended this match.

Mixed Doubles Final 210

The result of the Mixed Doubles Final: The Japanese Miki and British Miss Langrishe defeated the British Austin and Miss Sheppard to win the championship.

Miki (Japan) 3-6 Austin (UK)

Langrishe (UK) 6-4, 6-0 Sheppard (UK). Following her victory over the American Jacobs, Langrishe continued to display excellent tennis in the mixed doubles, combining volleys and smashes with Miki's pressure, leaving the opponents helpless. Miss Sheppard was the weakest of the four, and the opponents focused their attacks on her. Although Austin occasionally intervened, it had little effect.
