Bai Hong Track and Field Team: Origin of the Memorial Service for Mr. Sun Duoqi 218

The Shanghai Bai Hong Track and Field Team is initiating a memorial service for Mr. Sun Duoqi, the team's secretary-general. The origin of the service is as follows:

Mr. Sun Duoqi, courtesy name Shuoren, was from Shouzhou, Anhui. He was honest, hardworking, and particularly fond of associating with the masses. In his youth, he studied at the Eighth Middle School in Jiangsu Province. Among all the students in the school, whether they knew him or not, there was no one who did not know his name. In the tenth year of the Republic of China, he was admitted to the Shanghai Postal Administration, where he currently serves as a postal worker in the parcel department. In his interactions with people, he retained the demeanor of a scholar. Among all his colleagues in the bureau, whether they knew him or not, there was practically no one who did not know his name. Such was his sociability. In the autumn of the nineteenth year of the Republic of China, the Shanghai Bai Hong Track and Field Team was formally established. In its early stages, the scale was relatively small, and he was elected as secretary. In the twentieth year, the team's charter was revised, and the position of secretary-general was added. He was elected to that position. Subsequently, there was an election every year, and everyone considered him an indispensable talent for the team. In particular, the position of secretary-general, as the backbone of the staff committee, was responsible for practical matters. He was re-elected for five consecutive terms, enduring immense hardship. Zhuge Liang was diligent in serving the royal cause, with the saying "exerting every effort until death." Mr. Sun's dedication to Bai Hong was a fulfillment of these words. How sorrowful. We, his colleagues, recall the difficulty of organizing the team, clearing thorns and weeds together from the beginning, and realizing that there were few who shared our success. We feel even more keenly the enormity of his responsibility and the greatness of his contribution. Therefore, we initiate this memorial service for Mr. Sun, simply to do what we can to ease our hearts. We, his colleagues, have worked with Mr. Sun for several years, and some of us may not be fully aware of his admirable words and deeds. Here, we will briefly describe his dedication to the team from the team's perspective, a brief history of his efforts for the team. The matters may involve trivial details, and omissions may be inevitable. However, from our perspective, revisiting the past and using it as a basis for remembrance is also to supplement any omissions in Mr. Sun's conduct. All team affairs were planned by the secretary-general, and Mr. Sun ran errands and did not avoid hardship. For example, when someone went to Beijing for a competition, the name of one athlete, Mr. So-and-so, was accidentally omitted during newspaper coverage. Mr. So-and-so thought it was intentional and sternly rebuked Mr. Sun with an angry tone. Mr. Sun still humbly apologized and tolerated the situation. Such was his ability to endure hardship and accept blame. The team's finances were very strained. Whenever there was a shortage, he would run around to raise funds. Many donors were touched by his sincerity and the rare dedication to promoting sports, so they were happy to contribute. The funds raised by Mr. Sun were substantial. Other expenses, such as those for team social events, negotiating international sporting events, hosting news reporters, hosting team members from other locations, and negotiating all kinds of expenses, were all paid by him. Also, at the beginning of the editing of the team's third annual journal, Mr. So-and-so initially agreed to help with all the printing costs, but after publication, Mr. So-and-so went back on his word. The team was therefore in debt. After several attempts to find a solution, there was still a balance owing. The team could not cover it. At that time, Mr. Sun had important matters at home and borrowed money from the bank at high interest under extremely difficult circumstances, and generously allocated the borrowed money to pay off the debt. His dedication to public service, his selflessness, and his putting public interest before private concerns were beyond the reach of ordinary people. Mr. Sun deeply felt that the maintenance of the team was not easy, so he preferred to endure hardship himself rather than burden the team. Thus, Mr. Sun was no less than a caretaker for the team. However, Mr. Sun was obese and suffered from heart disease, so he was not proficient in any field sports. However, he would occasionally participate in long-distance races. Although he was always the last, or perhaps dozens or even hundreds of steps behind the leaders, and many racers would stop halfway, he would always continue to move forward, completing the course before stopping. His perseverance was truly admirable. Although Mr. Sun himself was not an athlete, he deserves to be praised as a sports administration manager. At every Shanghai National Games, he was hired as the manager of the Chinese team. When the Fifth National Games were held in Nanjing in the twenty-second year, he was also selected as the manager of the Shanghai team. Therefore, in today's Chinese sports world, whether they knew him or not, there was almost no one who did not know his name. Alas, with his prime of life and dedication to serving the sports community, if he had continued to work hard and move forward, the future development of the sports community would have benefited immeasurably from Mr. Sun. But Heaven did not pity him and abruptly took his life. Mr. Sun's death is not only a major loss for the team but also a misfortune for Chinese sports figures. Mr. Sun's family is a prominent family in Anhui, and his brothers have made a name for themselves in the education field. They all maintain integrity and self-discipline. Mr. Sun's income from his postal work was sufficient for his livelihood, but he was fond of making friends and helping others in need, and he was thus in debt. He left behind a wife, a son, and a daughter in dire straits. If we could be granted financial assistance to support the orphans and widows, or bestow an epitaph to honor his grave, the benefit to Mr. Sun would be immense. Therefore, we attach this appeal. This is the announcement. Respectfully announced by all members of the Shanghai Bai Hong Track and Field Team.

Essays

The Fragrant Shadow Record of the Imperial Incense 219

— Originally Written by Princess Der Ling of Qing, Translated by Qin Shouou

Because Consort Jin was merely a (concubine) style of consort, and although Empress Longyu was an empress, she was not favored by the Empress Dowager. The details of this are truly complex and difficult to understand: logically, the Empress Dowager should have disliked Consort Zhen because Guangxu was too fond of Consort Zhen, so she should have been happy with Longyu, especially since Longyu was her own niece. However, she did not love Longyu! Large families are the most prone to quarrels, and in the palace, it was especially impossible for everyone to be harmonious. It's a strange thing!

The Empress Dowager was so indifferent and ruthless towards Guangxu, so why did she insist on taking him with her to Fengtian this time? We people knew almost all the reasons for this; even Guangxu himself understood. In a nutshell, it was that the Empress Dowager still did not trust him, fearing that after he was out of her sight, he would have some ill-intentioned plans. Therefore, no matter where the Empress Dowager went, she was always very worried and had to take this special political prisoner with her. Perhaps she also believed that Guangxu no longer had any ambition at this moment, but she was still worried that some of the courtiers might be like the Six Gentlemen, taking advantage of her departure from the capital to incite Guangxu and persuade him to use external force to take back the Empress Dowager's power. This concern was certainly quite possible; and the Empress Dowager's temperament was particularly fond of wielding power. Although she was already an esteemed Empress Dowager, and all her enjoyments were far above those of others, she was not satisfied. She felt that without real political power in her own hands, all the glory and wealth would be equal to zero. Therefore, she did not hesitate to take a great risk, regardless of the slander from all sides, and desperately clung to her power. I often saw her so restless day and night over a difficult political matter that I could not help but secretly wonder, what was the reason that she could enjoy this tirelessly for so long? (7-8)

Childhood Longings 220

— 19

Speaking of which, this seems almost like old news. When I was eight years old, I went to the private school, and every day after returning, I was always happy to have (after-school money). Thinking about it now, this amount is truly small and laughable, only three copper coins! However, accumulating it day by day and stringing it on a rope, after a long time, it could become a hundred coins, which I would give to my mother to keep for me. I seemed to have become a rich man.

The so-called snacks didn't require me to dig into my own pocket. Other small snacks are now somewhat vague. It seems that a zongzi candy cost one coin, right? Square cubes of dried tofu cost three coins for two pieces. Sometimes, I would add two coins to the day's after-school money and buy a flat, round pouch of dried tofu to eat heartily, but this already felt too extravagant!

Speaking of snacks, a bowl of large meat noodles costing twenty-four coins was a rare treat. (Crab Shell Yellow) pastries cost three coins each. Steamed buns were worth thirty coins for ten pieces. Tangyuan also cost three coins each. Thinking about it now, this is also very laughable: Tangyuan were usually served with five pieces per order, but my cousin had a small appetite, so whenever he went to the snack shop, he always carried a basket with an empty bowl to bring back the leftover meat filling or the entire tangyuan.

That year, my mother gave birth in the middle of the night, causing me to not sleep well all night. The next morning, as the east turned white, she took pity on me and told me to go to the shop to eat a bowl of chicken noodles, which cost forty-two coins.

(Writing calligraphy) was a required course in the private school. A sheet of bamboo paper costing three coins could be cut into sixteen pieces. My mother put it in an empty honey cake box, and I took one sheet each day, as if I were treasuring it.

The above is of course just some childhood longings. (I look around, but cannot go where I wish,) and only these longings still tug at my heart from time to time.

Water Wharf 221

— Xu Xiaoting

Here, there is no sound of ship whistles, no noise of market, quiet space, only the sound of water gurgling, and women pounding clothes, singing and responding, playing a very rhythmic glissando.

The water wharf is constructed of layers of brick steps built from the flat, sloping riverbank, women walking among them, going back and forth on the high and low levels, the frank situation is more comfortable and freehand than running up the stairs.

In small inland cities, whether villages or rural towns, there is neither the facility of running water nor the many artesian wells. Therefore, women regard the water wharf as the only good place to fetch water, pound clothes, wash rice, and wash vegetables.

Water buckets, clothing clubs, and baskets, blue children, are held in everyone's hands, with every evening, noon, the busiest, when a group of women gathered, from the ripple marks on the water level, aroused every giggle and coquettishness, and the Zhang family chief, the Li family's short, a variety of different conversations. Sometimes, because of the splashing of water and the competition for position, a live drama of mutual scolding can also be staged; the expressions on their faces, from the edge of the water village, fully reveal a kind of innocence that does not contain any of the hypocritical ills of the city.

The inland water wharf is indeed a good place for women to open open-air talk clubs; every noon and evening, I stroll there idly, the delicate voices of the women, agitating the strings of flowing water, often arousing a deep, unspeakable nostalgia in my heart.

A Scene of Restraining Suicide 222

— Yan Biguang

This is really a very interesting thing. The Wang family couple next door quarreled because of a casual disagreement. The man is a strong and powerful friend, so his wife is often grabbed by the hair and beaten.

However, when women are wronged, old-fashioned women still use the old method of one cry, two hunger strikes, and three hangings. Unlike modern women, who use the new method of one cry, two runs away, and three divorces. After the Wang family woman was wronged last time, she cried and went on a hunger strike, but her husband ignored her, so she proceeded to the third step: she took a rope and began to practice hanging herself in the room. Just as she was hanging high from the beam, somehow, her husband found out. He rushed into the room and slapped her three times. Although she received three slaps, she was very willing, because custom told her that you must give slaps to the person who hangs to death to drive away the god of death. Who knew that after her husband untied her, he tightened the neck rope, asking her if she wanted to die again? She originally wanted to scare her husband, but how could she know that her husband really wanted her to die, so she had to shake her head repeatedly, and the husband let her go. This time, also because of a quarrel, she wanted to hang herself but it didn’t work, so she changed to drowning herself! When she ran to the river, before she could jump into the water, she was caught by him again. He asked her, “Do you want to drown?” and grabbed her, dipping her into the water several times, and her stomach was filled with water. Her husband was not afraid of death, and from then on she never thought of dying again.

Random Thoughts 223

— Tianzai

Society is always a draft to be revised, and there will never be a time when it is satisfactory.

Chinese people love the beauty of neatness and want to collect (ten major crimes) when attacking people.

When flowers fall, pessimists feel sad for them, and optimists think that the time to bear fruit is not far away.

Those who can truly sacrifice should be like soap, dedicated to washing others, while disappearing themselves in the process.

The perfume in the city cannot cover the invisible stench.

Although the lights in the city are bright, they cannot illuminate the entire darkness of society.

Northeast Four Company Commanders 224

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Thirty-One: Three Battles, White Clothes Charge Snow Formations, Whole Battalion Sacrifices, Red Eyes Enter Gun Forests

The brothers rummaged through their pockets, and sure enough, there was a paper roll, which they handed to Ziqiang. When he looked at it, several large characters caught his eye first, which read, "Father's Safe Greeting." These words were truly no less than the enemy's bayonet, stabbing him in the heart, and Ziqiang fainted again. In a daze, he heard a roll call, which was precisely for the brothers of his company. Then he heard Baofang say: "Brothers, we believe in ourselves and are not stupid, having won two battles and made our country proud. I have always said that the brothers led by me, Baofang, are all good friends, and now it's proven. What are we afraid of? There are still more than three hundred of us, and we can still fight the devils for a while. We are good stock, guarding this village, not leaving, waiting for reinforcements to come and hand over the village to them, and then we will advance! Brothers..." Baofang had not finished this speech when there was a deafening bang, and a cannonball came, not knowing where it landed, shaking the entire ground inside the fort. Ziqiang was lying on the pit, but his mind was very clear. He was thinking that the enemy's reinforcements must have arrived, and they wanted to take advantage of the Chinese army's rest and use fresh troops to attack the city again. This was a very vicious method. Just as he was thinking this, he heard a sound of footsteps outside the house, and also heard a very calm voice assigning tasks, clearly that the brothers had just begun to prepare for battle again. After six or seven minutes, he heard a second crash, and another cannonball landed in the fort. At this time, Ziqiang could not bear it any longer. He propped himself up and climbed to the window made of clay bricks to look outside. Sure enough, he saw the brothers carrying ammunition boxes and running up the fortress wall one after another. At the same time, the artillery fire was continuously being fired into the fort. On this side, apart from machine guns, there were no heavier weapons. So even though they were constantly threatened by the enemy's artillery fire, they could only endure it and wait quietly for the enemy to arrive, and then tear them apart. (429)

Social Sketches

— Xianxian

Catching Tooth Worms 225

An old woman was suffering from a toothache, not closing her eyes all night. The next morning, she waited at the entrance of the alley for a woman who catches tooth worms. She felt as if she had found a living deity, overjoyed and jumping for joy. She quickly invited her into the kitchen. After some haggling, both parties agreed that each tooth worm caught would cost one copper coin. It was said that the woman took pity on the old woman eating home meals, so the fee was particularly low.

Having agreed on the price per worm, the tooth worm catcher took out a yellow paper talisman from her cloth bag under her arm and burned it. She ordered the old woman to swallow it with clear water. Then, from her cloth bag, she took out a wooden hairpin, thick at the end and thin at the tip. She stirred the tip of the hairpin in a packet of gray powder for a while and began to perform her magic in the old woman's mouth. First, she pricked the old woman's gums, covering her teeth with bloodstains. Then, from the bleeding area, she caught tooth worms and placed them in a water bowl.

The more worms she caught, the more there were. Before long, she had caught over fifty worms, floating in the water bowl. Although each worm was only about half the size of a sesame seed, looking at them was enough to make one's hair stand on end. Over fifty worms, at one copper coin each, already required more than five hundred large coins, yet the woman kept catching them. The old woman, feeling the pain in her wallet and becoming suspicious, told her to stop catching them and gave the worm catcher a two-cent silver coin. Afterwards, she took a closer look at the tooth worms in the bowl and found that they were actually seeds that had burst open. She hurriedly went to chase the tooth worm catcher, but she had vanished without a trace.

Following this, another full night was spent without closing her eyes.

Female Teahouse Worker 226

One evening, I was dragged by a friend to a certain amusement park.

After sitting down in a certain area, a female teahouse worker brought over two cups of chrysanthemum tea. Then, she brought over two face towels.

My friend, accustomed to this sort of thing, reached out and pulled the female teahouse worker onto the empty chair next to him. The female teahouse worker had an expression of feigned resistance. My friend began to ask her name and where she was from. After some time of fooling around, the female teahouse worker's facial expression changed drastically, becoming talkative and smiling.

When leaving, my friend threw her a dollar and whispered, "Open a room." The female teahouse worker smiled back and whispered, "I can't leave until one o'clock." My friend continued, "I'll wait for you at the XX Hotel. Just ask for Mr. XX in room number X when you arrive."

Leaving the amusement park gate, I bid farewell and went home. A week later, I met my friend again and asked him about that night.

"That female teahouse worker was very cheap, but not very clean. I caught a venereal disease," my friend said with a mournful face. A few days later, I went to find my friend for something, but it was said that he had been hospitalized due to the illness.

Character Diviner 227

Character diviners in Shanghai can truly be considered a profession outside of the three hundred and sixty trades. The nature of character diviners is originally that of itinerant performers, possessing a wandering nature, but the character diviners in Shanghai all have fixed locations. Those who set up shop on a certain road, at a certain corner, or at the entrance of a certain alley always set up shop on that certain road, at that certain corner, or at the entrance of that certain alley.

The character diviners in Shanghai also inevitably display signs for "King Wen's Divine Oracle" and "Fortune and Fate," but discussing luck and misfortune is not the main business of Shanghai character diviners. Their real income comes from writing letters for people. For example, small merchants and workers who can't write themselves need to consult character diviners to write letters to their "dear parents" or "virtuous wife" at home. Old women working as maids in Shanghai who need to write letters to their "husband" farming in the countryside are also naturally the character diviner's regular customers. Business cards cost two hundred cash, letters cost at least ten cents, stationery and envelopes are extra, and postage is self-provided. Character diviners are not responsible for unclear addresses or incorrect names, whether the letter is delivered or not.

In addition, writing betrothal cards, loan receipts, separation agreements for lovers, and red paper strips with "Heaven, Earth, Emperor, Emperor" are all good business. Relying on "fortune and fate" can only lead to starvation.

Supplement to the Medical Weekly of Shenbao

Continued Discussion of Typhoid Fever, Part 2 (Middle) 228

— Yu Yunxiu

Wei also said: "The Foot Yangming Stomach receives the surface evil of the Foot Taiyang. The disease transforms into heat and enters the interior. Because the defensive qi and nutritive qi at the exterior originally originate from the stomach, the heat evil can enter the stomach through the collaterals of the stomach via the defensive qi and nutritive qi. If the disease is in the stomach, it should be treated. If the Hand Yangming Large Intestine is affected by the evil, it does not necessarily need to be treated." This takes the transmission from Taiyang to Yangming as originating from the defensive qi and nutritive qi entering the stomach's collaterals. Ke Yunbo, on the other hand, said that the heart governs nutritive qi, and the lungs govern defensive qi. Wind and cold invading the defensive qi and nutritive qi immediately affects the hand meridians. Alas, the defensive qi and nutritive qi are a single entity. Wei uses them to explain the transmission of typhoid fever to the Foot Yangming Stomach. Ke uses them to refute that injury to the foot does not injure the hand. It can be seen that unfounded words can be quoted in any aspect. Their insignificance is evident. In short, without recognizing what the defensive qi and nutritive qi actually are, without thoroughly investigating their boundaries, arbitrarily choosing what benefits one's own argument, quoting and using it, one can indulge in rhetoric and overturn heaven and earth. It is not merely a matter of far-fetched medical theories. As for saying that evil entering the large intestine does not necessarily need to be treated, this is truly a reckless statement.

Wei also said: "The Foot Shaoyang Gallbladder is originally the life force of the azure sky. All the qi of the body, whether evil or righteous, ascends through the Shaoyang. Therefore, evil in the intestines and stomach that wants to ascend must transmit to the gallbladder. If the disease is in the gallbladder, the Hand Shaoyang Sanjiao... Because it is formless, it borrows the form of the body's shell as its form, so it cannot specifically receive transmitted disease evil." This saying is even more vague and does not need to be discussed.

Wei also said: "If the evil of Shaoyang does not ascend and dissipate but transmits to the interior, it is like wood catching fire. Its smoke must be thrown into moisture... If the Hand Taiyin Lung is affected by evil, it does not necessarily need to be specifically treated." This purely establishes a theory based on the five elements. The theory of the five elements is already deemed incorrect by today's old medical community, so there is no need for me to harp on it.

Wei also said: "The Foot Shaoyin is below, using water to support earth. Its evil is most easily entered. If evil enters the Foot Shaoyin, then the Foot Shaoyin is treated. As for the Hand Shaoyin Heart Meridian, unless evil directly attacks the heart, no matter what the disease, it does not receive evil. All are replaced by the Hand Pericardium and do not need to be treated." The saying of water supporting earth is also based on the five elements and does not need to be discussed. As for saying that the heart does not receive evil, today's typhoid fever often results in death due to heart weakness. Evil's ability to directly attack the heart is definitely substantiated. The saying of the monarch not being attacked is merely an imagination under a monarchical system.

Wei also said: "If the Foot Shaoyin receives evil, whether cold or heat, it all transmits to the Foot Jueyin Liver. There is fire in water, and its qi, whether evil or righteous, must ascend along wood. If the disease is in the liver, the treatment must be in the liver. As for the Hand Jueyin Pericardium, it only replaces the heart in receiving disease and does not receive evil from other meridians." The saying of fire in kidney water comes from Daoism. Fire must ascend along wood. It is a forced interpretation of the Book of Changes and all belongs to empty speculation. Taking the kidney as water and the liver as wood is merely the saying of a school of Han Confucianism and is even more absurd. The saying of the pericardium replacing the heart in receiving disease is as unfounded as the saying of the heart not receiving evil. None of Wei's arguments are correct.

In short, Fang establishes a theory based on yin and yang, and Wei uses the five elements as a theory. Neither is sufficient to prove that the transmission of typhoid fever through the meridians is a truth, and even less sufficient to prove that speaking only of the foot meridians and not of the hand meridians is a fact.

After Fang and Wei, the one who wants to find a new life in the six meridians is Ke Yunbo of Cixi. Ke's approach is: "Zhongjing divides the exterior, interior, yin, and yang of all diseases into six meridians, clarifying the differences and similarities of pulse and syndrome, and the deficiency and excess of cold and heat, so that the treatment of disease is only within the six meridians. If the diseases of the body are all governed by the six meridians, it is like the six officials of the Zhou Rites managing all functions. As for typhoid fever, it is merely one syndrome within the six meridians. Shuhe did not understand that Zhongjing's six meridians are meridians of strategy, not meridians of channels. He rashly used the Treatise on Febrile Diseases of the Inner Canon as a preface and confused the syndromes and treatments of the six meridians. The six meridians of febrile diseases specifically focus on the meridians as the site of disease... Zhongjing's six meridians divide the area of ground. What they encompass is broad, including wind, cold, dampness, heat, internal injury, external affection, from exterior to interior, cold, heat, deficiency, and excess. Therefore, the outlines of the six meridians each establish a system, not restricted by the meridians of channels and not defined by wind and cold." This intends to find a place to stand for the six meridians outside the meridians of channels. It does not follow Fang's theory of the layers of yin and yang, nor does it adopt Wei's theory of the nature and principles of the five elements. Instead, it uniquely takes the evidence of the disease's syndrome as the explanation. However, what it calls the area of ground still cannot escape the old nest of the meridians of channels. Therefore, the ancients were undecided like playing chess. Examining its theory of the area of ground in detail, one can know that what it holds lacks a strong and unyielding special quality.

A Discussion on the Placenta and Umbilical Cord (Part 1) 229

— Qu Shaoheng

The Shanghai Times on June 25, 1934, published:

An Old Man Fantasizes about Rejuvenation by Eating Placenta. Grandson is Often Sick, Daughter-in-Law Complains, Accusing Son of Disrespect. The author is quite interested in this news item and believes that it is necessary to conduct detailed research on society, medicine, and law. I will now list my personal views on the left. I hope that comrades will correct them.

(1) Old Theories About the Placenta

The placenta, commonly known as the fetal membrane, is called "human placenta" or "Purple River Cart" in ancient medical books. It is also called "Chaotic Garment." It treats weakness and fatigue of qi and blood, and damage from labor in women. It also treats all kinds of postpartum damage. There are ancient formulas such as River Cart Pills and Great Creation Pills. It is just that the production is extremely difficult, so few people use it.

(2) The Composition of the Placenta and Its Effects on the Fetus

The placenta is a flat, oval, spongy disc-like object formed by the decidua basalis and the chorionic membrane. It is rich in blood vessels and has a bluish-red color. It first appears in the second month of pregnancy and is completed in the fourth month of pregnancy. The placenta at the end of pregnancy has a diameter of 15 to 20 centimeters. However, its thickness, edges, and fetus are like the ashes after smoking.

(4) Biological Research on the Placenta

Since Luthude and Larrierll discovered a specific PlassroidaleKugel in Syncytium cells in 1901, it has been considered a product of endocrine secretion, and the theory that the placenta has an endocrine effect has been advocated.

In 1904, Halbor stated that changes in the genitals during pregnancy, hair growth, the mammary glands of newborns, the uterus, mammary glands, and menstruation were all the result of stimulation by placental products. Buchaeart also advocated that the placenta has the effect of promoting milk secretion. Based on his own experimental results, those who supported his opinion included Lederer, Prjibsani, Mayer, and the Japanese scholar Dohi. Clypon initially refuted it but later agreed. However, according to the results of experiments by Ott, Scott, Ascherer, Crigorin, Herimann, and the Japanese scholar Taniguchi using the corpus luteum of the ovary; Hochstatter using the pituitary gland; Ott, Scott using the pineal gland and thyroid gland; and Schaefer, Mackensjie using the postpartum uterus, all obtained the same galactagogue effect as the placenta. Therefore, it is believed that the galactagogue effect of the placenta is not unique to the placenta but is a common component contained in the organs. The Japanese scholar Hirose's research on the placental emulsion, which has a proven effect of promoting mammary gland development, is quite detailed.

Yellow Plum Season and Lung Disease 230

— Shen De

It is generally known that winter is not suitable for the treatment of lung disease. In cold weather, the climate is dry, and the airways are prone to inflammation, causing colds and coughs, which have a negative impact on lung disease. However, there is less rain in winter, and there are more opportunities to perform outdoor air therapy. When the weather is cold, patients and caregivers are extra cautious. Therefore, as a result, fewer lung disease patients experience aggravation in winter. This is not the case in summer, especially during the yellow plum season, which is even more unfavorable for lung disease. Symptoms that are gradually recovering, such as fever and hemoptysis, often recur during this period. When the temperature is hot and the humidity is high, even healthy people feel uncomfortable, so the impact on patients is naturally even greater.

From my own experience, I often feel tired for no reason in the summer. Sometimes, I feel unwell all over and don't know where to place myself. Many critically ill lung disease patients in the hospital also die in the summer. Therefore, I believe that the yellow plum season and summer are the times when lung disease patients should pay the most attention to treatment.

The principles of treating lung disease are nothing more than rest, fresh air, and adequate food. Among these, rest is the most important. Overwork is most harmful to lung disease. Therefore, those with lung disease should be careful everywhere and not allow their bodies to feel tired. It is too late to rest after feeling tired.

In the city, except for those who live in the suburbs, it is difficult to obtain fresh air. Shanghai, in particular, has a dense population and poor air quality, which is worse than other places. Therefore, the wealthy

Newspaper Medical Advertisements 231

— Song Guobin

Medicine is a tool for preserving life, but if used improperly, it is more than enough to kill. Therefore, for non-doctors to practice medicine and for non-doctors to use medicine are both extremely dangerous. Ordinary newspapers in European and American countries never publish any medical advertisements because the nature of advertisements is often exaggerated and untrue, and the general public lacks the ability to judge medicine. Once allowed to publish them extensively, both quack doctors and quack medicines can use a small space in the newspaper to sell their monopolistic sales tactics, and the public with simple knowledge will be shocked by their rhetoric, rush to them like ducks, buy them without hesitation, and fall into their trap without realizing it. To prevent their malpractices and eliminate their dangers, to save the public from confusion, to cut off the path of quack propaganda, and to prevent the tools of life from turning into instruments of death, this is what enlightened journalists in our country should deeply consider and carefully plan.

(Editor's note) This journal has always been extremely strict with medical advertisements, and the advertisements in this supplement are even stricter. Because medicine concerns life, it is necessary to pay serious attention to it.

The Hygiene of Academic Instruction and Physical Examinations of Children (Part 1) 232

— Cheng Hanzhang

(Manuscript of a speech given at the Public Education Hall on July 8)

Today, I am honored to be invited by the director of the Shanghai Public Education Hall to speak at your hall about children's hygiene. I, as a humble person, have been very busy with my practice in the past few days and have not had any free time to devote to society, which I am very ashamed of. However, it was difficult to refuse the kind invitation, so I have made some time today to ramble on a bit.

Today, I will be talking about the hygiene of academic instruction and physical examinations of children. This is a very important issue regarding children's bodies and their future happiness as adults. At the same time, it is also something that our great educators keep in mind at all times and want to do practically. We must know that being able to appropriately apply hygienic methods during education has a great positive impact on the physical and mental development of children in school, which goes without saying. Therefore, school hygiene books often discuss in detail the hygienic methods to be used when teaching various subjects.

First, the Hygiene of Academic Instruction

The most important thing to pay attention to during teaching is whether the children's posture is correct. The first element of posture is that the chest develops equally on both the left and right sides. The chest of a newborn is absolutely different from that of an adult. The spine of a newborn is a straight line without curvature, and the ribs are perpendicular to the spine. The chest wall formed by the ribs is cylindrical, much like a wooden barrel used to hold cement. When the child is able to walk, the chest initially bears the weight of the head, and then the weight of the internal organs and its own weight, so the front wall is pulled downward. The ribs tend to slant forward and downward to the spine. At that time, the spine curves to a certain extent due to the center of gravity. For these reasons, the chest gradually becomes flat, and the cross-section of the adult chest becomes oval, and the spine protrudes forward. This kind of chest is the foundation of our entire trunk and the main part of posture.

The body's posture should be symmetrical from front to back and left to right, and the development of the limbs should also be appropriate. However, upon close study, our human bodies are not symmetrical from left to right. The outer corners of the eyes are not on the same horizontal line; the shapes of the left and right nostrils are also different; the thickness of the left and right limbs are also different. Even the chest is different on the left and right sides. After carefully measuring the height of the two shoulders, there are also some differences. The reason for this asymmetry is due to the position of the internal organs and the amount of habitual exercise and labor in daily life. If the degree is deep, then the position and function of the internal organs will be greatly affected. This will become a bad posture. Many children develop spinal curvature (such as hunchback) and chest deformities because their parents do not provide reasonable care and upbringing during their childhood. The most common chest deformities are left-right asymmetry, funnel chest, pigeon chest, barrel chest, atrophic chest, and localized protrusion of the chest. We collectively call these many deformities bad posture. In schools, we must train children to practice hygiene and prevent the formation of bad posture, which is the foundation for cultivating healthy citizens. Especially during subjects such as reading, writing, drawing, arithmetic, and work, children are most prone to adopting a hunchbacked posture. At this time, we should pay full attention to them.

Speaking of reading and writing, these are things that children in our schools do every day. Writing in our country is especially more complicated than in foreign countries. They have to write both Chinese characters and Western letters, and sometimes they have to write phonetic symbols. The writing tools used include brush pens, pencils, slate pencils, and fountain pens. There are also chalks. With such a variety of tasks to do every day, the chances of developing abnormal body postures are very high. How can we not pay full attention to it?

Third, Physical Examination

Schools must spend a few days at the beginning of each semester to conduct physical examinations for students. In addition, there are also temporary physical examinations conducted for various purposes. Why do educators willingly sacrifice so much precious time to do this work? That is to say, conducting physical examinations for children every year can provide them with valuable records and statistics on health protection or health promotion. However, now, in many schools, due to time constraints, complete and ideal physical examinations are not being conducted for most students, which is a great pity.

(A) The Value of Physical Examination We can divide education into two goals: mental and physical. Physical education is physical education. And physical examination is also part of the physical education category. The result is, of course, to further pursue appropriate educational methods, such as dividing children into two categories, physically weak and strong, after the physical examination, and implementing appropriate physical education separately. For those with developmental or nutritional deficiencies, we need to study ways to help development and improve nutrition. For those with defects or diseases, we should provide correction and treatment.

A Brief Discussion on Pulmonary Tuberculosis (11) 233

— Hu Jiayan

Chapter 4: The Evolution of Pulmonary Tuberculosis

What is exudative inflammation? It is characterized by exudate. This cause is entirely due to changes in the blood vessel walls; at that time, the blood vessel lumen dilates, and the components of the blood also exude out of the vessel walls. In this way, the surrounding tissues are infiltrated, and the local area exhibits redness, swelling, and heat. This process is called (exudation); the blood cells and fluid exuded from the blood vessels are what Gang Xian called (exudate). This kind of blood cell is mostly multinucleated white blood cells. This kind of exudative inflammation also differs in terms of the nature and state of the exudate, and pathological changes, with various distinctions such as serous, catarrhal, hemorrhagic, purulent, and putrefactive. The states within these are certainly very specialized, so I will omit them all.

The second type is proliferative inflammation, which is also commonly called productive. It is characterized by the proliferation of connective tissue. The components of this proliferative tissue, in addition to newly formed capillaries, also produce various cells. This state is mostly a phenomenon of healing for each type of inflammation; however, it is also possible for this change to appear at the time of onset. Having clarified the general situation of exudative and proliferative inflammation, we can then proceed further and talk about the changes that occur in the tissues of the human body in tuberculosis (strictly speaking, pulmonary tuberculosis). We must know that once tubercle bacilli invade the human body, they develop and reproduce in it, resulting in the formation of a hard nodule, which is the (tubercle) that everyone knows. It is composed of granulation tissue; it does not contain blood vessels, or at least, it can be said that blood vessels are very scarce; therefore, the nutrition inside is often lacking. As a result, it is easy to become (necrotic).

Common Sense on Ear, Nose, Throat and Eye Hygiene (Continued) 234

— Tang Renzeng

(4) Discussing an Eye Disease Originating from Gonorrhea

The occurrence of ophthalmia neonatorum in newborns usually happens on the third or fifth day after birth. Its transmission is not directly infected in the birth canal, but indirectly infected after delivery. However, if the puerperal woman does not have gonorrhea, the newborn will not have the chance of infection. Speaking of its danger, although it is less dangerous than adult gonorrheal ophthalmia, it is also easy to cure if treated properly. However, things are not always like this in reality, because by the time they seek medical attention, the dangers mentioned above have already occurred, inevitably leading to the tragic result of blindness. I remember when I visited a school for the blind in Germany, I learned that 30% to over 50% of blind children lost their sight due to ophthalmia neonatorum. Furthermore, according to a survey by a certain medical expert, among the 1,040 people who became blind in the first year of life, as many as 753 people were due to ophthalmia neonatorum. Looking at it this way, ophthalmia neonatorum is as dangerous and frightening as adult gonorrheal ophthalmia, which can also prove the close relationship between gonorrhea and eye diseases. This disease is best treated in hospital with isolation. Never let self-proclaimed doctors with superficial knowledge treat it indiscriminately, otherwise, once the treatment period is missed, blindness will be inevitable. Now I will talk about the prevention methods for this disease in detail. If it can be implemented, it may be a safe approach.

(A) For those who already have gonorrhea: (1) Whether male or female, when suffering from gonorrhea, a formal specialist doctor should be consulted immediately for diagnosis and treatment. Do not delay. (2) Before eating and washing your face, and after urination, wash your hands thoroughly with carbolic soap. Do not directly infect your own eyes. (3) Do not wash your clothes and pants with others.

(B) For those who do not have gonorrhea: (1) Do not get too close to people who already have gonorrhea. (2) Use public towels less often. (3) Prohibit unclean sexual intercourse, which can reduce the chance of indirect infection.

(C) Prevention of ophthalmia neonatorum in newborns: This is something that obstetricians or midwives should do. In European and American countries and Japan, there are already mandatory regulations in the law. I don't know if our country has this law. However, general formal obstetricians and midwives have already implemented this law. The method of this law is based on the method created by Crede in 1882. This method is to wash the whole body and face of the child after delivery, and then instill 2% silver nitrate solution into both eyes. Speaking of the prevention of ophthalmia neonatorum, it can be said to be very effective. Recently, some people have switched to using drugs like 10% to 20% silver proteinate, such as Targesin, Protangel, etc. Their efficacy is also good. However, there are many midwives in our country. I don't know if they use this prevention method. This belongs to the matter of health administration. I am not in a position to criticize anything. I can only hope... (To be continued)

Free Talk

On the South Manchuria Railway Line 235

— Li Huiying

When you get on the South Manchuria Railway train, everyone will have a few common feelings: that the train is very clean, the ride is smooth, and there are rarely crowded passengers.

However, you will always have an opposite feeling: that you are not sitting on a train, but a poor little bird living under someone else's roof. The owner of the train is a big eagle, always opening its mouth wide, ready to swallow you into its big belly.

Therefore, the first few feelings result in us admiring the seriousness with which others handle affairs, achieving good results, while the latter feeling makes those of us who enjoy the benefits feel ashamed and uneasy, with a certain sense of unease and lack of freedom.

Going south from Changchun, the road is full of vast plains, which is part of the Guandong Plain geographically. Sipingjie is the largest station between Changchun and Shenyang, and also a collection point for grain, fur, and hides. The Siping-Taonan Railway stretches its long neck to the border of Inner Mongolia, swallowing a bellyful of grain, fur, and hides, and transporting them to Dalian trainload after trainload. At the same time, farmers in northern Liaoning and southwestern Jilin also drive large carts pulled by four or six horses at the end of the year to transport grain to this place for sale. However, before the railway was opened, it is said that Tieling replaced Sipingjie's position.

Further south, the soil is mostly red. The main agricultural product along the line is sorghum, because this is the main staple food of the people of Liaoning. However, since last year, people on the train have not been able to see the green stems and red spikes within twenty li. This is because the Japanese are afraid that the Volunteer Army is hiding in the fields. South of Liaoyang, north of Haicheng, and Anshan Station must be specially mentioned, because there is a very large (exactly how large is impossible to say) (Anshan Iron and Steel Works,) few iron and steel works in Japan can compare with it. Sitting on the train, in the morning or evening, you will see cheap Chinese laborers carrying baskets, going to and from work on both sides, walking like beads, wearing yellow and thin faces. They are all slaves who have left the fields and gone to the iron factory to sell their blood and sweat to Japanese imperialism. They can only do ordinary work. It is said that some secret work is all done by the Japanese themselves. What exactly they are doing is impossible for outsiders to say, but because it is an iron and steel factory, people can still imagine that nine out of ten things are secretly manufacturing lethal weapons.

South of this, there are gradually more mountains, but they are all bald, and their decadent appearance is like a beggar lacking clothes and food in winter. When you get to Wafangdian Station, the situation is different. The mountains gradually increase, and each mountain is covered with green pine clothes. Even on the rocky mountains, there are still green pines everywhere, but the pine branches are slightly shorter, which is due to the later planting time. South of Jinzhou, there are many fruits along the road, especially apples. The scope of sales has already broken through the South Manchuria Railway line and spread throughout the entire Northeast. This item alone, apple income, adds a large amount of income to the Japanese every year. It is very convenient to eat on the South Manchuria train, because there are people who specialize in selling snacks on the train, all of which are Japanese goods, but they are all very clean. Eight out of ten passengers are our compatriots.

Now every station is surrounded by heavy barbed wire fences, which can be said to be a new construction after the September 18th Incident. Also, the piles of sand piled up at the station are all new products to prevent attacks by the Volunteer Army.

The Farmer's Life in the Poet's Mind 236

— Cao Juren

Opening the third issue of the "Fiction Semi-Monthly," I saw Mr. Yu Dafu's handwritten poem about what he saw on the road in Lin'an:

(Four or five houses with mud walls and thatched roofs, two or three camellia buds just sprouting; when the weather is fine, men and women are busy farming, leaving the flowers in front of the door idle.) I can't help but think of Lu Fangweng's poems and Xin Jiaxuan's lyrics. This relaxed rural scenery, like the March breeze, makes everyone have thoughts beyond the dust. But I come from the countryside and know a lot about rural affairs. This poetic rural sketch is all a fantasy of the literati.

It has been very dry for months, and the waterwheels should be very busy. The literati imagine: a crescent moon, a few scattered stars, a cool breeze gently blowing, and a thin dew soaking your clothes. At this time, holding the horizontal bar and stepping on the treadle, the sound of the waterwheel and the singing intertwine, what a poetic thing this is! An ancient poem says: (The gentle breeze sends the sound of the treadle,) how can it not make people yearn for it! However, this twist will turn out to the conclusion that (there is a big mistake)! The body of the waterwheel must be made of extremely fine and hard wood, because the body of the wheel is sometimes immersed in water and sometimes exposed to the sun. If you don't use this kind of wood, it will easily crack. The treadle and the wheel have to carry three or five people, so they also have to be made of fine and hard wood. The whole waterwheel is heavy and heavy. Four poets cannot lift a wheel body, and three pairs of literary giants cannot carry a wheel. Water pumping is often done by streamside ponds, high streamside banks, deep pond water, (two people wheel) is not up to the task; is often a dozen feet tall wheels (four or five people wheel) erected there. When there is a lot of water, four or five people step on the water at the same time, step by step, like carrying a thousand kilograms of load, simply can't be lazy; sweat dripping, panting, the soles of the feet are hot and blistered, but you have to step on it step by step. The water level has gone down, and the body of the wheel is light, but the rice seedlings, which are being fertilized, are more urgent than a baby drinking milk. Looking at the dry streams and ponds makes people even more anxious. The streams and ponds are dry, and the only source of water can only rely on the mountain spring at the bottom of the ground. Dig a deep hole in the ground, and wait for three or five hours for the spring to fill a small pool. This spring water is more valuable than gold. Sometimes the ground is high and the water is small; the coupled wheels can't be hoisted up, and you can only watch the rice fields wither and burn, and you have to sigh! My father, when he was alive, talked about how my ancestor was lonely and poor in his youth. When the weather was dry, he pumped water, and he couldn't do it. My grandmother used both hands to help him. Pointing and showing each other, tears were like rain. Late at night, every time I heard the sound of the wheel, it was like a ghost wailing, so sad that I couldn't bear to listen. Unfortunately, this kind of real feeling has never been written into the poet's pen!

Li Shangyin's poem: (Stop the car and lie down to watch the maple forest at dusk, the frosted leaves are redder than the flowers in February.) Watching the red leaves in the autumn mountains, the high and refreshing sky, set off by the fiery frosted leaves, there is a great interest in this. Red leaves, especially the leaves of the tallow tree, are the most beautiful; its leaves are denser than maple leaves. Once the cold frost falls, the tallow leaves change suddenly, light yellow and deep red, mixed together; covering the mountains and fields, dyed into a large picture; poets also like to write this into the poem. However, the farmers have never taken these red leaves seriously; once the red leaves fall, the tallow seeds are ripe, and the silvery tallow seeds are cracked from the black and shiny ones. Big and small, male and female, everyone goes to the mountains and fields to pick tallow seeds; tallow oil is used to light lamps, tallow shells are used to make fire, and tallow cakes are used to fertilize the fields. The farmers regard this as an income in winter. Speaking of collecting tallow seeds, I am terrified; there is a kind of hairy caterpillar on the tallow tree, even after heavy frost, it is still alive, and almost every tree has it. Once a worm touches the body, it itches and blisters, and the pain is unbearable; burning rice straw to smoke it also takes four or five hours to return to normal; or use vegetable oil and salt to rub it all over, it hurts slightly; at this time, even if there are ten buckets of poetic feelings, it will turn into a hundred liters of anger! The year before last, in the countryside of Zhenru, I saw a red tallow tree, and I couldn't help but feel homesick; I also thought of the hairy caterpillars, and my heart was cold; the bitter hairy caterpillars once a year, this is also something that poets did not expect when chanting red leaves.

Watching lotus and picking lotus in summer is a refined thing. The lotus blossoms emerging from the water are delicate and dripping; the lotus leaves are fragrant; the human world and the heaven, this scene is the same. The new lotus is fresh and tender, and it is sweet and soft when it enters the mouth, and it is even more delicious. (Picking lotus and picking lotus again, the lotus leaves are so lush.) The farmers in the lotus bushes are no less than immortals. Good, then please ask the poet to pick lotus! The lotus stalks are full of fine thorns. Where the feet pass, they cut the thighs like a knife. Once you pick lotus, it is like being slowly sliced to death. There are many leeches in the water, stinging the thighs and sucking blood, often causing itchiness; and you can't pull them out immediately, otherwise the head will break into the skin and invade the blood vessels. These kinds of situations are also far beyond the poet's imagination!

Therefore, after reading Mr. Yu Dafu's impromptu poems, I can't help but think of Mr. Lu Xun's "Storm":

(Old men and men sit on low benches, shaking large plantain fans and chatting idly, children run like flying, or squat under the tallow trees and gamble with stones. Women bring out dark steamed dried vegetables and pine flower yellow rice, steaming with heat. Literary people's wine boats sail in the river; when literary giants see it, they are filled with poetic inspiration and say: (Without worries, this is really a rural paradise.)

But the words of the literary giants are somewhat inconsistent with the facts, just because they have not heard the words of Old Woman Jiujin. ... )

Unfair Words 237

— Cao Huchu

I just can't understand, a hundred, a thousand, ten thousand can't understand: are there no other people in our village? Why do you have to let Wang the old man be the village chief!

Grandpa Li next door said that Old Man Wang is a scholar, a Xiucai from the Qing Dynasty. In our village, his qualifications are the oldest, and his reputation is the greatest. Naturally, he is worthy of being the village chief.

Humph! Scholar! What is the use of a scholar? Scholars only know how to eat, not how to farm; only know how to pace, not how to walk long distances; only know how to shake their heads and hum a few rotten tunes, not how to do things honestly. Their bodies are as thin as dried eggplants, and their arms are as thin as dry firewood sticks. Don't say going to fight foreigners, we don't need them. Even if we call them to fight Zhang Ersao at the entrance of the village, they will shout for help. The boss of the small shop at the bridgehead said the day before yesterday; (China is so poor and bullied by foreigners to this point, it is really because there are too many scholars; because most of the scholars in China only know how to eat idly, put on airs, read a few dead books, and are unwilling to do things honestly.) Thinking about this carefully, there is some truth to it.

Humph! Old Man Wang is a scholar, let's see what skills he has? People say that he has read a lot of books, his belly is very open, and he can write good characters. In the southern villages, he is counted as the number one or number two old brand Xiucai. Humph! What's the use of having an open belly if you don't know how to do things? What's the use of writing well, only knowing how to make a splash by stamping a few signatures on everyone's land deeds, not knowing how to hold a hoe and dig the ground? If everyone in our village were like him and did nothing, didn't know how to hold a hoe and dig the ground, even if the Heavenly Lord pitied us and gave us good weather all year round, the fields would be barren and withered, and everyone would be starving ghosts. Humph! Old Man Wang is worthy of being the village chief, really the heavens have no eyes, everyone respects him, pats his ass, but I am not convinced.

Granny Li said: (Scholars know reason, and besides, Mr. Wang is a famous Xiucai in the southern villages. If we don't respect him and let him sit in the chair of village chief, who else is qualified.)

Humph! What does the old woman know! I don't believe the saying that scholars know reason either. Isn't the old gentleman Guo in the county a scholar from a family of books and incense with a great reputation? Why did he plot to seize the property of his widowed sister-in-law in March of the old year, causing his sister-in-law to commit suicide by drowning! The teacher in the Dongcun school is of course a scholar. Why did he also skim off the top when handling the land declaration a few years ago, stuffing the public money into his own pocket, and sitting in jail for three months! In the old year, the second little boss of the landlord where I worked, wasn't he a college graduate? Why didn't he do some business properly, but insisted on being a partner with gangsters, indulging in prostitution and gambling all day long, and as a result, he was driven away by his father, who refused to recognize him as his son? Do you say that Old Man Wang is a scholar who knows reason? Since he is the village chief, how can he only know how to lick the boots of the county officials, bureau chiefs, and big gentry in the city, and not know anything about running the village? He doesn't care if the village has a bad harvest; he doesn't care if people in the village are infected with the plague; he doesn't care even more if robbers come to the village. These are still acceptable, but he hides by the opium lamp every day, scraping his guts for oil, planning how to rip off someone, planning how to skim off a bit of oil; planning how to flatter his superiors; planning how to hang on a woman's arm... Is this kind of low-down behavior considered reasonable?

Ah! Ah! Speaking of women, it really makes my stomach burst with anger! Yesterday I was chatting with Sister Agui under the big tree at Nanhetou, and this old thief saw it. He actually lectured me, saying that I shouldn't be flirting with women, and if I did it again next time, he would definitely send me to the Public Security Bureau. His mother! He doesn't touch his own ass, but instead lectures me! Who doesn't know about his early years, who doesn't know? I am a bachelor, and Sister Agui is an old maid who is almost thirty years old. Everyone chatting about love is not a big deal. Besides, we have never had any sneaky affairs except for talking a few words when we meet; he, who is worse than beasts, is always more decent. Is it possible that because he is a scholar, a Xiucai, a village chief, he can act recklessly, do whatever he wants, and consider low-down behavior to be proper and reasonable? Is it possible that we poor people chatting a few words with the people we love in the sun during the day is considered a crime? His mother! At that time, if I wasn't afraid of scaring Sister Agui, I would definitely give that shameless old thief a few slaps in the face!

In a word: it is really absurd that Old Man Wang, a person like that, is worthy of being the village chief, a hundred, a thousand, ten thousand absurd! Others respect him and pat his ass, but I just don't agree; if I run into him, I won't give him a few white eyes unless heaven and earth turn upside down. Anyway, I don't want to rely on his signboard and don't want to eat a grain of his rice.

You Give Me a Slice of Melon, I'll Give You a Fan 238

— TK

Swindlers (2) 239

— Cao Ming

My companion let out a mocking laugh in the next room, and I quickly broke free from her hand, deliberately shouting in a low voice when running out of the room (Female swindler, what a powerful female home wrecker!)

I don't know why God always calls me to run into those troublesome women.

It was my fifth year as a policeman, and at that time I was a squad leader. The fourth district chief was originally preparing to promote me to police chief. But because of a stupid thing, I had to suffer for two more years. But it's still considered that God has eyes, there are many people who have been policemen for twenty years and are still getting 80% of their wages.

That was a very unusual woman, her mouth as sharp as a sword! It was probably around noon in June of the previous year. I had just started work not long ago. A crowd of people surrounded the entrance of Pingxi Lane in Xiajiufu. I strode in with my police baton as usual. A thin woman with a sallow complexion in her thirties was sitting cross-legged against the wall, holding an infant covered in rags like a dried monkey in her hands, with some bloodstains on the little head. People believed that she had just given birth, so many coppers and coins stood quietly around the woman; I suddenly became very smart and understood in my heart that something must have happened. So I bent down and said to the woman:

(Can you walk?) She nodded reluctantly. So I took her all the way to the (Chengxi Convenient Hospital).

(Do poor people need to go to the hospital?) When she got to the entrance of the hospital, she hesitated and said, I explained to her and dragged her in.
