Economic Supplement Published Every Monday Issue 80

Methods for Compiling Import Tariffs 240

— Ye Zixiu

Import tariffs have the effect of restricting import trade, hence the term "tariff barriers" used by commentators. In reality, this analogy is not entirely accurate; rather than calling them barriers, it's better to call them sluice gates. This is because the function of tariffs is not only to restrict trade but also to regulate it, just like sluice gates regulate water flow. Building a sluice gate requires considerable skill; it's not just about being tall and large. Compiling tariffs is much the same. Since China achieved tariff autonomy, tax rates have repeatedly increased. When discussing tariffs, most Chinese people focus on the level of tax rates, seemingly paying less attention to the structure of the tariff itself. Therefore, I will briefly describe the methods for compiling tariffs.

The work steps for compiling tariffs can generally be divided into four categories: (Classification), (Categorization), (Formalization), and (Rate Setting).

(1) "Classification" refers to the process of categorizing the myriad of goods into a specific system based on their nature. This ensures that everything is well-organized, without omissions, and with minimal overlap. There are approximately four types of classification methods: by tax rate (high or low), by alphabetical order, by the production system, or by the use of the goods. The first two methods are simpler and can only be used when the number of items is small. The latter two methods are more precise and are commonly used in tariffs. However, each has its advantages and disadvantages. If classification is purely based on the production system, ordinary bulk goods, from raw materials to finished products, can have a fixed and unchangeable sequence, but semi-finished products pose a challenge. If classification is based on usage, there is no difficulty with miscellaneous products, but for goods with multiple uses, it is difficult to decide which category to place them in. Therefore, most tariffs usually consider both aspects and make slight modifications. The methods of modification vary greatly depending on the circumstances of each country. For example, if a certain product is a major import in one country, it may be designated as a separate category to show importance. If another country rarely imports it, this is not necessary. Furthermore, if a product is used as food in country A but only as an industrial raw material in country B, the classification results will naturally differ. The former International Economic Conference made a suggestion to standardize the tariff classifications of various countries. Although the principle was approved, it ultimately failed, for this very reason.

(2) "Categorization" refers to dividing an item into several categories based on its characteristics, aiming to adjust tax rates or facilitate differential treatment. Regarding differential treatment, some items within the same category can be manufactured domestically, while others cannot. Some are mostly imported from country A, and others are mostly imported from country B. To devise appropriate countermeasures, it is essential to distinguish them clearly. Regarding adjusting tax rates, the prices of superior and inferior goods within the same category may vary greatly. Applying the same tax rate would unfairly burden one more than the other. For example, if the value of a certain item varies from one to ten dollars per unit, and the tax rate is set at one dollar, the rate on the superior goods is only 10% of their value, while the rate on inferior goods reaches 100%. In this situation, it is necessary to divide the item into several categories and assign appropriate tax rates to each. The criteria for categorization may be based on size, weight, length, price, or the special characteristics of the item, such as the yarn count of cotton yarn, the thread count of fabric, the optical rotation of sugar, the alcohol content of wine, and so on. It is important to have clear and definite boundaries. Sometimes, an item can be divided in multiple ways. Determining the most suitable method depends on the specific needs. Moreover, for the sake of necessity, there are times when one knowingly chooses not to categorize even though it is possible. For example, if the low-end products within a certain item can be manufactured domestically, while the high-end products cannot yet be manufactured, then, under appropriate circumstances, applying the same tax rate regardless of quality can avoid hindering the trade of high-end products while restricting the import of low-end products, which is not unfeasible. Therefore, categorization is not about quantity; complexity that precisely meets needs is the best choice.

(3) "Formalization" refers to stipulating the form of the tax rate. There are approximately four forms of tax rates: (Ad Valorem), (Specific), (Ad Valorem and Specific), and (Ad Valorem or Specific). "Ad Valorem" is calculated based on the value of the goods, regardless of quantity, such as silk at 100% of its value and coarse grains at 10% of its value. "Specific" is calculated based on the quantity of the goods, regardless of price, such as handkerchiefs at 30 cents per dozen and buttons at 6 cents per gross. Each of these two forms has its advantages and disadvantages, which can generally be distinguished in three ways. First, in terms of equitable burden, ad valorem taxes are clearly more flexible, avoiding the situation of being disproportionately light or heavy. Specific taxes, on the other hand, have the opposite effect. No matter how precise the categorization, there will inevitably be a situation where high-value goods are taxed lightly and low-value goods are taxed heavily within the same category, though the difference will be smaller with more precise categorization. Second, in terms of tax administration, the advantages and disadvantages are reversed. Specific taxes are simple to collect, while ad valorem taxes are prone to disputes over valuation, and the amount of tax revenue is subject to fluctuations in prices, which is particularly inconvenient. Third, in terms of protection effectiveness, specific taxes are reliable and certain. The difference between domestic and foreign prices is fixed and unchangeable. Conversely, ad valorem taxes often change with the price of goods. If the price increases, the tax rate increases, which may excessively hinder trade. If the price decreases, the tax rate decreases, which can easily be exploited by those who dump goods. For example, if the original price of a certain item is ten dollars per unit and the ad valorem tax is 40% of its value, the tax is four dollars. If the price rises to fifteen dollars, 40% of its value would be six dollars. If the price increase is already difficult to reconcile, raising the tax rate is like adding insult to injury. Conversely, if the price falls to five dollars, 40% of its value is only two dollars. If the price falls to two and a half dollars, 40% of its value is only one dollar. If the sharp price reduction is already intolerable for domestic manufacturers, the tax rate is also invisibly reduced, which is like adding wings to a tiger. Since both ad valorem and specific taxes have their advantages and disadvantages, some combine these two forms, which is (Ad Valorem and Specific). For example, a felt hat is three dollars per dozen plus 20% of its value. There are two tax rates. This form can have the advantages of both ad valorem and specific taxes, but also inherits the disadvantages of both, and the calculation is more complex. However, the tax rate gradually increases with the rise in the price of goods and gradually decreases with the fall in the price of goods. It is neither as inflexible as specific taxes nor as extreme as ad valorem taxes. Within a reasonable range, it benefits tax revenue, which other forms cannot match. As for the (Ad Valorem or Specific) form, both ad valorem and specific tax rates are listed, and the higher one is adopted (the lower one is rarely adopted, because the power of choice will shift to the merchants). For example, a felt hat is 40% of its value ad valorem, but not less than five dollars per dozen. This form is ad valorem for high-end goods and specific for low-end goods, which does not hinder the trade of high-end goods while preventing the influx of cheap goods, making it most effective in protecting emerging industries. In addition to the above four forms, there are also so-called (Sliding Scale Tariffs) and (Quota Tariffs). (Sliding Scale Tariffs) vary their tax rates according to seasonal changes or price fluctuations, with the aim of regulating production and sales and equalizing prices. They are mostly applied to agricultural products. For example, fruit tariffs are raised during the autumn harvest and lowered during the lean season. Similarly, grain tariffs are raised when domestic prices are low and lowered or waived when prices are high. (Quota Tariffs) stipulate the annual or quarterly import quantity. Imports within the quantity limit are subject to a lower tax rate, and the tax rate is raised or imports are prohibited after the quota is met. The aim is also to protect industries, and they are mostly applied to industrial products. Upon closer examination of the nature of these two tax rates, the different tax rates are not implemented simultaneously. However, the increase or decrease in tax rates is more flexible than ordinary revisions. The form of the tax rate still falls within the four categories listed above. The variations of tax rate forms are roughly as described above. As for which one should actually be adopted, there is no definite method. It can be said that specific taxes are suitable for bulk goods with similar prices, while ad valorem taxes are suitable for scattered goods with significant price differences. If the intention is to protect industries or prevent the dumping of cheap goods, the forms of (Specific) and (Ad Valorem or Specific) should be used as much as possible. If the intention is to increase fiscal revenue and the percentage tax rate is very high, the forms of (Ad Valorem) or (Ad Valorem and Specific) can be used.

(4) "Rate Setting" refers to setting the specific numerical values of the tax rates. The setting methods can be roughly divided into (Direct) and (Indirect). The (Direct Method) directly stipulates the tax amount per unit. The level of the numerical value is determined by comparing the production costs or sales prices of imported and domestic products. The main aim of this method is to protect industries from undue pressure from imported products. The increase or decrease in tax revenue is not given much importance. The (Indirect Method) first stipulates the level of percentage for each category of goods. For example, the tax rate for luxury goods should be high, the tax rate for necessities should be low, the tax rate for manufactured luxury goods should be the highest, and the tax rate for essential raw materials should be the lowest. If the form of the tax rate is not suitable for ad valorem, it is converted based on the standard dutiable value. For example, if the percentage for a certain product is set at 30% of its value, and the standard price is twenty dollars per unit, then the specific tax rate should be six dollars. The calculation of the standard dutiable value is based on the domestic market price, with a deduction for tax rates and commissions, or based on the foreign market price, with an addition for freight and other items, depending on the circumstances. In theory, both methods aim to obtain the price of the goods when they arrive at the customs, and the principles are not different. However, regardless of which method is used to calculate the price, the results must be adjusted. There are two meanings to adjusting prices. First, there are many types of goods. No matter how precise the categorization, it is impossible to give each brand a single tax rate. Different brands with varying prices are grouped into one category, and the change in the sales volume of each brand is sufficient to affect the rise and fall of the average price. This rise and fall is not a real rise and fall in the price of goods. It is difficult to take it as a standard when calculating tax rates. Otherwise, the sales volume of high and low brands will often change, and the tax rate will also increase and decrease repeatedly, which is meaningless. Second, comparing the prices of each category, there may be abnormal and unreasonable prices. For example, imported processed goods may be mostly low-end, while unprocessed goods may be mostly high-end. If the specific tax rate is calculated based on actual figures, the tax rate for processed goods may be lower than that for unprocessed goods, which is fundamentally inconsistent with the principles of setting tax rates. In this situation, even if the calculated price is known to be reliable, the price of processed goods must be appropriately raised, or the price of unprocessed goods must be appropriately lowered. Once the price has been adjusted, the calculated tax rate cannot be without discrepancies. Those who do not understand the actual situation may point out that the valuation is inconsistent, but it is actually limited by the facts and there is no other choice. To avoid this kind of entanglement, a (Comparative Addition Method) can be adopted, which transcends the price of the goods. It stipulates that processed goods should be taxed according to unprocessed goods, with an additional amount. The additional amount may be a percentage of the value of the goods, or a percentage of the tax rate of the unprocessed goods, or a specific form of a certain amount per unit. This additional method can be said to be a variation of adopting a direct rate-setting method within an indirect rate-setting method. The above is a rough explanation of the two types of rate-setting methods, direct and indirect. Generally, the indirect method is applicable to ordinary goods, and the direct method is applicable to a small number of special items. The former is extensive, the latter is precise; the former is stable, the latter is concise; the former is like the first draft of a drawing, outlining the distribution of tax rates, while the latter is a detailed description of a certain part. The tariff items are numerous, and studying them in detail is not possible in practice. Where to apply direct methods for precise calculation, where to use indirect methods for a rough approximation, or to make slight modifications, all depend on the tariff policy. However, the so-called tariff policy is nothing more than deducing from the facts. In terms of protecting industries, it seems that the higher the tax rate, the better. However, excessive protection only increases the burden on consumers, leading to the drawbacks of shoddy manufacturing, or even hindering the development of other industries. In terms of tax revenue, it seems obvious that an increase in the tax rate leads to more tax revenue, but this is not always the case. If the tax rate is increased excessively, the import quantity may decrease, or it may lead to smuggling and tax evasion. Not only does the tax revenue not increase, but it may even decrease. Therefore, setting tax rates must first have a considerable understanding of the domestic and foreign production and sales conditions, and then consider the situation of producers, consumers, administration, and tax revenue. Choose a suitable position from the lowest tax-free point to the highest prohibitive point. Even if it is not possible to reach the precise point where an increase of one point is impossible and a decrease of one point is impossible, there should be a considerable calculation. Otherwise, relying solely on intuition and acting arbitrarily, there are few who do not fail.

The Process of National Import Tariffs 241

— Guang

When the National Government announced tariff autonomy on July 23, 1927, a Provisional Regulation on National Import Tariffs was drafted, scheduled to be implemented on July 1. However, Britain and Japan were the first to oppose it, and it was not implemented. In June 1928, the country was unified. The National Government, realizing the ineffectiveness of merely declaring tariff autonomy, changed its policy and sought to achieve tariff autonomy through treaty revision. Therefore, it adopted two methods, abolishing treaties and revising treaties, and proceeded separately. After negotiations, various countries gradually complied. The treaties signed by the National Government with various countries in 1928 are listed below:

Treaty for the Adjustment of Tariff Relations Between the United States and China… July 25, 1928

Sino-German Treaty… August 17, 1928

Sino-Norwegian Tariff Treaty… November 12, 1928

Sino-Polish Tariff Treaty… November 19, 1928

Sino-Swedish Tariff Treaty… December 20, 1928

Sino-British Tariff Treaty… December 20, 1928

Sino-French Tariff Treaty… December 22, 1928

Tariff Clauses of the Sino-Belgian Treaty… November 22, 1928

Tariff Clauses of the Sino-Italian Treaty… November 27, 1928

Tariff Clauses of the Sino-Danish Treaty… December 12, 1928

Tariff Clauses of the Sino-Portuguese Treaty… December 12, 1928

Tariff Clauses of the Sino-Spanish Treaty… December 27, 1928

Since the National Government had signed tariff clauses with various countries, tariff autonomy could have been realized sooner. However, Japan made things difficult, causing delays for a very long time, with almost no results. China then based on the relatively easy-to-implement seven different tax rates, and set a transitional tax rate, which is the Customs Import Tariff promulgated on December 7, 1928, and decided to be implemented from February 1, 1929. In May 1930, China and Japan signed a reciprocal tariff agreement. The National Tariff Commission then recompiled the new tariff, which the National Government promulgated on December 29, 1930, and implemented from January 1 of the following year.

In May 1933, when the three-year term of the Sino-Japanese Reciprocal Tariff Agreement expired, the Chinese authorities, in view of the actual needs, revised and reorganized the 1930 import tariff in its entirety, which took effect on May 22.

This revised national import tariff was able to express the spirit of tariff autonomy. The tax rates for cotton cloth and its products, rayon and its products, aquatic products, tobacco and alcohol, and other goods were specially increased. The tax rates for rayon and alcohol were increased from 30-50% to 80%. The tax rates for various fish and seafood products were increased by an average of more than two times.

Up to June of this year, in order to protect domestic industry and commerce and maintain international trade, the Chinese financial authorities have increased or decreased the customs import tariff, which has been revised and promulgated by the National Government and implemented on July 2. The classification number of the new tariff is the same as before, with no changes. The increases and decreases in the new tax rates for various goods are listed below:

Japan's Trade with China 243

— Pei

Japan's trade with China has traditionally been dominated by cotton goods, sugar, paper, cotton yarn, wheat flour, machinery, and aquatic products. Since the Great War, there haven't been significant shifts. Among these, cotton goods have consistently ranked first among goods exported to China, except for 1928. Sugar, paper, and wheat flour compete for the second position. Coal and steel are also major commodities. The following is a table illustrating the changes in Japan's exports to China:

Regarding the past two years, cotton goods were the top Japanese export to China in 1931, totaling 65,257,731 gold units, accounting for 72% of China's total cotton goods imports and 24.8% of Japan's total cotton goods exports. This illustrates the significant role of cotton goods in both China's cotton goods import trade and Japan's cotton goods export trade. Paper products were second, totaling 16,826,371 gold units, accounting for 43.5% of China's total paper imports. Sugar was third, totaling 15,938,965 gold units. Following these were wheat flour, coal, cotton, machinery, electrical materials, aquatic products, rice, and timber. In 1932, affected by the September 18th Incident and the January 28th Incident, Japanese cotton goods exports to China significantly decreased, amounting to only 38,284,523 gold units, but still maintained the top position among Japanese goods exported to China. Wheat flour was second, totaling 8,234,889 gold units. The subsequent order was sugar, paper, steel, aquatic products, coal, cotton, timber, rayon, and machinery. Generally, compared to 1931, all showed a sharp decline. A detailed table is provided below:

Securities: Bond Market Soars Last Week丨New High Prices Appear Continuously丨 245

From July 2nd to July 7th last week, the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange only conducted four days of trading, excluding Monday and Tuesday due to exchange settlement. Starting from the 4th, afternoon trading was suspended due to the scorching weather. The brisk trading and high market conditions were unprecedented. The anticipated high prices were reached within a day or two, exceeding the expectations of short sellers and the desires of long buyers. The ability of consolidated salt tax bonds to surge after reaching a 70% discount, abruptly and fiercely, was truly beyond the norm. Short sellers who sold at high prices consistently failed. Although there were various reasons such as the Ministry of Finance's inventory check, the 1996 reorganization, the Ping-Shen railway opening, and Sino-Japanese peace talks, these were all common knowledge and not new developments. The rumors of a new Sino-American loan agreement and the establishment of new tariff rates, along with Premier Wang's formal talks on reorganizing domestic and foreign debt, were more influential than previous rumors. As the balance continued to accumulate, short sellers increased, leading to successive surges in prices. As prices increased, some short sellers covered their positions, while others sold off, causing prices to rise even further. The eagerness of short sellers led to repeated surges, almost forgetting the high discount, creating a peak effect. New high prices seemed endless. In the near future, a sharp decline is unlikely, as market sentiment remains highly enthusiastic. Last week, Monday and Tuesday were settlement days with no trading. On Wednesday, after the market reopened, prices were relatively stable, showing signs of consolidation. On Thursday, half-day trading began, coinciding with rumors of the 1996 reorganization, boosting market sentiment. The 1996 bonds surged by over one yuan. The upward trend continued on Friday, with buyers showing no hesitation and prices rising sharply by several cents to about two yuan. On Saturday, the upward momentum remained strong, with various bonds reaching new highs. The surge was remarkable, with 1996 bonds rising sharply by over two yuan. As a result, the week saw gains ranging from over one yuan to over four yuan, with a total transaction volume of 87,675,000 yuan. The results are listed below:

Oil Market: Ji Feng Ying Hong Tong Oil Opens 249

Ji Feng Ying Hong Oil, produced in Changde, is known for its exquisite color. Although its history is not long, its sales have spread throughout the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, covering a wide area. The production volume this year is similar to last year. The first batch of 2,000 to 3,000 pieces was sold at a price above 23 yuan. Yesterday, another batch opened at a price of 22.8 yuan, with approximately 1,100 pieces sold, slightly cheaper than the first batch. This was not what the merchants initially desired, but due to the severe drought, sales may not be strong in the short term. Therefore, they made slight adjustments to stimulate the interest of buyers, which is a common strategy. However, as it is currently a busy time for farming, farmers are focusing all their efforts on watering and irrigating their fields and may not have the capacity for other activities. It is feared that strong tung oil sales will only occur after a significant rainfall. The quantity of goods taken in by local firms in recent days has not been large, so they are not in a hurry to sell, only preparing to build up their inventory.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

On the "China-Japan Brothers" Theory 251

— Ming Tang

The newspaper reports Yan Huiqing's remarks, saying that he once told the Japanese that China and Japan are brothers, and the only major yellow-skinned countries existing in the East are China and Japan. Therefore, they should cooperate to achieve coexistence and co-prosperity. In terms of race, China and Japan are indeed brothers; the major yellow-skinned countries existing in the East are indeed China and Japan, and they are also the only remaining yellow-skinned countries. In terms of race, China and Japan should indeed help each other to achieve coexistence and co-prosperity. Even the Japanese often shout that China and Japan should coexist and co-prosper, but the result is that the Japanese hope to dominate East Asia, overwhelm the Chinese people, and achieve the sole existence and prosperity of their country. How did this come about?

In theory and in practice, China and Japan should cooperate to promote the development of East Asians in East Asia. However, the Japanese insist on oppressing the Chinese people, talking about some kind of East Asian Monroe Doctrine, allowing this vast China to be solely dominated by them. There is a definite reason for this. The reason is that a small number of wealthy Japanese, nobles, and superiors hope to obtain a larger source of wealth in China to seek the so-called development of their empire. This is why they want to monopolize China. These few wealthy Japanese, nobles, and superiors, because they have exploited the people enough in their own country, and the dying Japanese farmers and laborers can no longer be exploited by them, therefore, the clever wealthy Japanese and others have to think of ways to exploit abroad. This is one of the motives for their invasion abroad. Furthermore, the increase in the status of wealthy Japanese is also necessarily linked to external exploitation in principle. This is also a definite fact. Therefore, the fact that Japanese (of course, a minority) oppress the Chinese is determined by definite historical reasons. It is not that some Japanese are bad, or that the Chinese should be specially exploited, but the relationship of money that forces them to do so. Understanding this, the so-called racial views have absolutely nothing to do with it.

The Japanese invasion of China is entirely for the sake of money. Therefore, whether the Japanese and Chinese are brothers, how to be brothers, what kind of people are brothers, and whether the so-called brothers should be distinguished by money are all questions that can be completely understood. That is to say, the so-called brothers should definitely be distinguished by money. The majority of the Japanese people (the awakened people) are oppressed and deceived by a small number of wealthy Japanese. Similarly, the majority of the Chinese people are also oppressed and deceived by a small number of wealthy Japanese. In this way, from the standpoint of being oppressed and deceived, the majority of the Chinese people and the majority of the Japanese people can become brothers and friends. In fact, this is indeed the case. Conversely, a small number of wealthy Japanese and a small number of Japanese warlords who live by money, if they can suddenly realize and not invade the Chinese people, not oppress and deceive the Chinese people, and make no distinction between countries, can also become brothers. But I wonder if it is possible?

Teahouses in Guangzhou 252

— He Juefu

Anyone who has been to Guangzhou must have a deep impression of the teahouses in Guangzhou!

Speaking of the teahouses in Guangzhou, there are so many that it is really hard to count. You can find them everywhere, whether on the streets or in the alleys. Even in the nearby villages, you can often find two or three thatched tea sheds.

In Guangzhou, drinking tea has become a fashion among the people there, and it can also be said to be an indispensable expense in the daily lives of a group of people. Even if you are not a big fan of drinking tea, as long as you live there for three or five weeks, I guarantee you will gradually be assimilated by them and become addicted.

With so many teahouses and so many people drinking tea, someone who doesn't know the real situation in Guangzhou would surely think that the lives of the people there are so comfortable. But the actual situation is not as beautiful as imagined. The abundance of teahouses and the large number of customers only reveal the boredom and monotony of the lives of the people there. Because a group of people without a proper job and without a lot of money think that (time) is worthless, even worse than getting through it. Since they feel painful to be trapped alone in their lodgings and do not have much money to go to the major entertainment venues to have fun, they have no choice but to go to a teahouse, invite two or three friends to chat and drink tea, and pass the boring years. Moreover, the facilities in Guangzhou's teahouses seem to be designed specifically for these people. In front of every teahouse, there must be a stall renting out all kinds of newspapers, large and small; the seats in each teahouse are so many that it is impossible to count them all. No matter how many hours you sit there, the boss will never show any sign of wanting you to leave; some even set up a stage in the middle of the guest seats and hire one or two actresses and a band to sing and play, for the enjoyment of the customers. As long as you spend a dime or two, rent one or two newspapers, order a pot of tea, a plate of melon seeds, and a plate of snacks, you can leisurely and comfortably drink tea, shell melon seeds, read the newspaper, and listen to music all day long. Who wouldn't enjoy such a life?

If it is a sweltering hot day, the business of the teahouse will be even busier. Because teahouses are mostly skyscrapers, the air is cooler, and there are also electric fans spinning non-stop. If one's pockets weren't empty, who would want to be confined in a small lodging and suffer from the heat?

It wouldn't be much of an exaggeration to say that Guangzhou's teahouses are the headquarters of the middle class without a fixed occupation! Because that's where the majority of them are.

Page 22

In the Sweltering Heat 253

— Chen Liang

Four or five men, bare-chested, their backs scorched red, beads of sweat hanging all around their heads, hanging down to their necks, shoulders, chests... There, a thick rope was thrown around the base of their necks, heavy, seemingly embedded into the flesh. Under the scorching sun, they were going up the bridge, (Pull! Pull!) The one behind, blocking the wheels, shouted desperately, his throat about to explode! The four or five in front glanced at each other, frowning (If we pull ourselves to death, that's it.) Everyone resented in their hearts, they had to eat, there was no other way to think.

A pile of steel bars, scorched hot by the sun, the iron wheels pressed against the melting asphalt bridge surface, stuck fast and couldn't move. They used all their strength, almost pushing their heads to the ground, every vein strained taut under their skin. Their shorts were soaked through with sweat. The trolleybus followed closely behind, ringing its bell, and behind that was a car, a grass-green body, a cream-colored awning, a steel spare tire cover, a three-toned horn, the most popular sports car of the summer.

It just sat there idling, the scorching sun not reaching the people in the car. The people in the car were so lucky. They shouted:

(What's going on? Why is the car in front stopping all the time!) It was a woman's shrill voice.

(Maybe another car broke down.) A man replied gently.

(It'll be late getting to Wusong.)

(It'll be cooler at night!)

A hand in a white glove gripped the steering wheel, an American-style straw hat rested on the side, a starched shirt clung snugly to his chest, in the style of a movie star, a Chevrolet smile pasted on his face, and a strong Chesterfield burned at the corner of his mouth. The other hand stretched behind the woman's back,

rolling a pair of talkative eyes.

She leaned wearily against the spring leather cushions, a pair of two-inch-long earrings dangling;

(Darling, can't we get past them?

I can't stand the heat coming in from the street.)

As if receiving an imperial edict, the car crept past the trolleybus as the steering wheel turned. The iron wheels of the cart had just started to move when the head of the one pulling the cart at the front was smashed in by the car, spurting crimson, hot blood, blood, blood... under the intense sun.

The injured one rolled to the side of the bridge, the uninjured ones stopped the car, wiping the sweat from their foreheads into the car, stretching their thick, black arms in front of their faces, (Pay for his life! Pay for his life! Pay for his life!)

He naturally threw away the cigarette butt (Call the police!)

A policeman squeezed into the crowd, with no surprised expression on his face. He calmly took out a notebook, (What to do? Go to the station together, or...?)

Then he took out a card (If there's anything, you can notify us.)

(But, sir, you have to send the injured person to the hospital.)

(Well... please figure it out. We can't waste our time.)

Saying that, the engine roared under his feet, and without a single word of apology, he drove off.

The policeman clipped the card into his notebook and hired a rickshaw to take the injured person to the hospital, under the scorching sun.

Those who weren't hit still had to pull, the wheels rolling over the purple bloodstains on the asphalt (Pull! Pull!) Glancing at each other, frowning (If we pull ourselves to death, that's it.) Everyone resented in their hearts, they had to eat, there was no other way to think.

On Jungong Road, the evening breeze blew in summer, the sweltering heat had retreated, and leisurely yachts floated in the Huangpu River.

The car, with its green body, cream-colored awning, and three-toned horn, the hand in the white glove gripped the steering wheel, the man, with a Chevrolet smile on his face, the woman, with her wandering, talkative eyes:

(Darling, can't you drive a little faster?)

Summer Vacation Bewilderment 254

— Bulu

According to reports: This summer, college graduates in Peiping, unable to bear the bewilderment after graduation, recently organized a "Vocational Movement Grand Alliance." The purpose of this alliance is roughly two points: (1) To defeat unemployment; (2) To indirectly hint at the need for reform of higher education.

In this situation of widespread unemployment, it seems that college students have no way out, which is a natural phenomenon. But if we examine it a little, we feel that this is somewhat ridiculous. We all know that our country is backward in everything. The main reason for this is the lack of talent. We also know that in our country, those who can study to graduate from college are all privileged individuals. According to the Ministry of Education's statistics, in proportion to the population, they account for only one person in every ten thousand. This is such a precious figure. It seems that society should make use of this batch of rare talents in some way. But in fact, the opposite is true. On the one hand, they are shouting that there is no talent, and on the other hand, talent is unemployed. This phenomenon cannot but be said to be ridiculous and incomprehensible.

Why is there such a contradiction? Here, we cannot but ask such an urgent question.

As far as schools are concerned, it is undeniable that the current Chinese education system is an education system that creates young masters and misses, an education system that is completely divorced from real society, and an education system that is consumption-oriented rather than production-oriented. The graduates created by this kind of education system spend several years and exchange it for a piece of paper, a diploma. The value only arises from the diploma, but the diploma cannot represent knowledge. With such talents, in the current stage of Chinese society, of course, there is no ability to assume any responsibility. However, a part of society that needs real talent still laments the difficulty of finding talent.

Let's talk about society. Like market monopolies and oligopolies under capitalism, any organization, under the leadership of someone, is completely dominated by his cronies. As long as they are from the same hometown, classmates, members of the same party, or relatives through marriage, they can all benefit from his blessings. On the other hand, if you want to find a job, without relying on the power of your parents and brothers, without relying on the recommendation of wealthy people, without relying on the assistance of people from the same hometown, classmates, and political party, without relying on the internal help of relatives through marriage, but only relying on your own real knowledge and training, then that is a dream. This is the real situation. The occupational distribution of this society is extremely uneven.

Of course, we cannot absolutely blame either side for the fact that college graduates have no way out, but looking around at the current reality in China, these two phenomena are expressed simultaneously in this society, which no one can deny.

In this way, the organization of this alliance by college graduates in Peiping is, in our opinion, a noteworthy event. At least, we express our full sympathy for the fact that they are taking responsibility for their own problems. For the two goals they put forward, defeating unemployment is of course the current urgent task of college graduates, and suggesting the reform of higher education is even more important for the future of China!

Little Yan's Sorrow 255

— Yi Ding

Time seemed to flow by like lightning. It had been a full eighteen years since Little Yan was bought into the Zhang family.

She was only thirty-six full months old from the time she was born in her mother's womb until she left home.

Therefore, Little Yan really knew very little about her family's affairs and her own life experience. Time was so short for her, what could she possibly know?

However, in her mind, there was still a vague impression:

On the vast land in the fields, leaning towards the south, wasn't there a cluster of deep green jungle? In this jungle, weren't there a few low, dilapidated thatched cottages? The one with a few pine trees in front of the door, that was her home.

What exactly did her father look like? She couldn't recognize him clearly, but there was a person of about forty years of age, with a face full of beard, hair that grew strangely long, tied into a braid on top of his head, a flat face, the color of which was yellowish and black.

Page 23

, like old orange peel, eyes that were sunken and without any brilliance, teeth that were dirty and yellow, and his mouth often emitted a kind of suffocating smell. He wasn't tall, but he wasn't considered short either, and he always wore this broken black cloth jacket. He spoke in a very heavy voice, liked to drink, often caused trouble, and seemed very fierce, but in reality, he wasn't like that.

Another woman, with a sad and bitter face all day long, that was her mother.

Her impression of her mother was relatively deep, and she seemed to have a special feeling for her mother. In her mother's body, she often smelled a kind of maternal scent. She loved her mother, liked her mother, because her mother directly raised her, loved her so much, cared for her, and comforted her.

Even now, she seemed to still remember her mother's face, her mother's voice, and the many songs that her mother often sang to her. She would never forget her mother. Little Yan felt that her mother was good, that her mother was so lovable!

However, this was only a vague impression. When Little Yan was so young, when she was picking up some scraps of information from her mother's mouth, it was also the time when her hometown suffered a terrible disaster. In order to support their two old lives, in order to pay off those debts that could never be paid off, her parents had no choice but to sell this, their only asset—Little Yan—to the Zhang family in town.

From that time on, they struggled with difficult and hard days. And Little Yan also gradually grew up in the Zhang family's relatively well-off living environment. At first, when she didn't understand the world, Little Yan was like a little bird, without restraint, soaring freely in the sky. The owner of the Zhang family loved her very much. Now that she had become an adult, she looked even better than when she was a child, and she knew more things.

Troubles and misfortunes then gradually, gradually approached her day by day.

The mistress began to have a kind of extreme jealousy towards her, so she especially abused her, ruined her, and made her live a life worse than that of cattle and horses day and night. And Master Zhang, on the other hand, had long harbored a wild ambition towards her, so behind his wife's back, he especially approached her, using sweet words and threats to seduce her, sparing no effort in his techniques.

At this moment, she was fighting with pain. From the mouth of the old nanny, she learned what kind of people the Zhang family were, learned about her situation, and learned about her terrible fate in the future. So she thought of her family, thought of her parents who were sold them their daughter because they were starving and freezing, and of the situation she herself was currently in, and couldn't help but feel a deep chill. She was determined to run away secretly, but where could she escape to? She hesitated, uncertain. There was no home, and she didn't know whether her parents were alive or dead. She might not even recognize them anymore.

Mother 256

— Jing Jia

Last night, I dreamed of my dead mother, just like she was alive, with a kind smile on her face.

Immediately, I seemed to know that I was in a dream, I seemed to know that this dream would soon wake up. I threw my body into her arms. Like a child, I looked up and sat on her face, my right index finger held in my lips, and I happily called out (Mom)!

Mother stroked my hair with her hand, and the faint, gentle, familiar lullaby echoed in my ears again.

(Mom, I want to be in your arms forever, hypnotized by the sweet sound of your song; seeing your kind smile. Mom, let's never be separated!)

Mother smiled slightly, without saying a word.

(Mom, my younger brother has grown up, and my younger sister can also jump and run. They are all so cute. Mom, do you know?)

Mother was still smiling, without answering.

(Mom, I have a lover! She is a beautiful girl. She can also laugh and sing. She has black hair and bright eyes! Mom, are you happy?)

Mother nodded with a smile.

I lowered my head and thought for a while, I was thinking of some happy things to report to my mother. My heart was full of happiness, and my throat was also filled with words. But, I couldn't say it... I smiled and didn't speak! I looked at my mother, and my mother also looked at me. Really, when had we ever been separated! Wasn't my mother still smiling so kindly?

(Mom, this must not be a dream!)

Then I woke up, my hand dragging the corner of the quilt.

Worse Than Death 258

— San Duo

Currently, dead people's heads are being sold in bulk on the market. We don't need to give examples. Just pay attention to the news about "death," and dead people's heads are moved to the market in the fastest spin cycle. First, to take advantage of the fact that customers still remember that this dead person's head is the latest, and second, dead people's heads will sell, each with different speeds, so it is first come, first served. Making a fortune from dead people is precisely the shortest path to wealth in a sluggish market. However, what is being bought and sold is (future contracts.) I once dreamed that if I really put this dead person's head on the market, the grand occasion would be even more imaginable, but the people who do magic tricks don't have that ability. Because they are Changshan comrades, they have to maintain the dignity of Changshan. If they nakedly sold dead people's heads, wouldn't they collapse the stage for Changshan comrades? So this good business was imitated by the duanshan comrades of another class, who dug up other people's ancestral graves.

It is said that the trend of kidnapping for ransom was wholesale imported from American movies to China. A pistol kidnaps a person without a trace. Such a good, once-and-for-all business is naturally something that the people of the gold-dollar country could not have imagined. However, since there is attack in the art of war, there must be defense. Therefore, those who are qualified to be kidnapped hire Russian bodyguards with pistols. In this way, although it is not certain that they will not be kidnapped, it is ultimately more difficult to do so.

This point is naturally where our Chinese are cleverer, digging up other people's ancestral graves. Since the dead don't know how to resist, and they don't have strict defenses, they put the bones of the dead anywhere and ask for hundreds of thousands of dollars, which is ten thousand times higher than selling dead people's heads with empty promises.

However, once this trend starts, many ancestral graves with status cannot be built in the dragon's veins of scenic places. Isn't this giving the bandits an opportunity? They should immediately move to the bustling areas of the concession, build high walls, build large buildings, hire bodyguards, and raise police dogs to prevent the theft of the bones of the dead!

Lan Jiabao's State of Mind (II) 260

— Xijun

Just whispering, whispering, whispering behind the black robe. Smoking, listening to a pair of hurried Tangos played on the flute, browsing the bright fleshy scenery in front. Sexual sensation received intense stimulation, becoming increasingly unbearable. To resist the outbreak of this malaise, he sometimes unconsciously closed his eyes. He only allowed his auditory senses to be intoxicated by a slow and graceful Waltz, and Karl had reached a point where he had to dance, he was simply mad, he said:

丨丨 Hey, let's have a pair.

丨丨 He's got the malaise again.

丨丨 It's better not to come than to sit here doing nothing!

The lights went out, and Karl opened the record first.

Karl usually exaggerates his sexual sublimation, but with an exquisite and smooth body in front of him, he can prevent sexual cells from blooming. But at this moment, he was once again a conquered prisoner, the charm of sensory pleasure!

Yes, those who are tired of struggling in the torrent of life all love to use this implicit form to seek the discharge of sexual appetite, just like us together. Almost every night is spent immersed in these places, these places full of rich colors. But when the music is gone, the singing is gone, shoulders slumped, listlessly wandering on the lonely road home, listening to the night wind whistling through the leaves of the plane trees, the leaves falling one by one to the ground, far away, near and far, only you are sending off the chirping of the crickets in the sunset of youth, slowly drifting away, drifting away, at this time, the taste of loneliness poured into the heart only one's own self knows!
